About this document

Purpose of the document
This document aims to enable both new and experienced users of the Arkite software to translate their
standard operating procedures into a project and as such configure their workstation. The manual
contains an overview of all basic and advanced software features.

Note
  • For instructions on installing and mounting the sensor, please refer to the Arkite hardware
    installation guide.
  • For instructions on installing the Arkite software, please refer to the Arkite software
    installation guide.
  • This document describes the features that are available in the 2025 .1 version of the Arkite
    software.

About the Arkite software

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

1. About the Arkite software Table of Contents

1.1 Purpose of the Arkite software

Arkite offers the ultimate operator guidance platform. It transforms workstations into a digital and
interactive environment.
The Arkite software allows you to configure the platform and adapt it to your specific working
environment. Through the Arkite software, you can translate your standard operating procedures into
a project without any programming knowledge.
Three license types are available for using Arkites Operator Guidance platform:

 Arkite Guide license:
Once your project has been configured, Arkites operator guidance platform will be able to provide
your operators with real-time picking and assembly instructions through Augmented Reality.
The system cannot verify if a step was done correctly. The operator will always have to confirm he
has executed a step and press the Next button on the touch screen, a hardware button or a foot
pedal to continue to the next step.
All features from this license are also included in the Arkite Validate and Arkite Vision licenses.
 Arkite Validate license:
When using this license, your Arkite Operator Guidance Platform is equipped with an Arkite 3D
sensor. The system will verify if a step is executed correctly. It will automatically continue to the
next step after a step has been done correctly, and will warn your operators in case of any error.
All features from this license are also included in the Arkite Vision license.
Throughout this document, features that are only available when a workstation is used in
combination with a sensor are tagged with a note Validate and Vision license only.

 Arkite Vision license :
When using this license, your Arkite Operator Guidance Platform is equipped with an additional
high definition infrared vision sensor. You can then benefit from Arkites smart vision features.
 Product inspection during assembly
 Improved presence detection for small objects (> 0,5 cm)

 Object orientation
Features that are only available when a workstation is used in combination with an Arkite Vision
sensor are tagged with a note Vision license only
Tip
For an overview of different applications of Arkites operator guidance platform, have a look at the
references on our website:
https://arkite.com/references/.

About the Arkite software

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

1.2 How does the Arkite 3D sensor work? (Validate and Vision license only)

Technology
The Arkite 3D sensor used by Arkites operator guidance platform is a Time-of-Flight sensor.
Combining this ToF-sensor with intelligent algorithms, the Arkite software can verify the presence of
objects and validate operating procedures.
The sensor uses two types of streams to capture data:

 Depth stream
 Infrared stream
By default, the Arkite software will automatically select the stream with the best contrast. However,
you can overrule this selection and force the software to use a specific stream.

Depth stream
The sensor is sending out infrared light, invisible to the human eye. The IR light reflects on all objects.
For each pixel, the time is measured for the light to travel from the sensor to the object and back. Then
the distance of each pixel to the sensor is calculated. This results in a 3D image or point cloud. Virtual
boxes are created on top of this real-world 3D image. The activity of an operator or the presence of an
object in the box will lead to a detection trigger. By combining all these triggers in the correct
sequence, the Arkite software can validate operating procedures.

Infrared stream
The reflected infrared light beams will also create an infrared image. The reflection intensity of each
pixel is measured. The more IR light is captured by a pixel, the higher the value will be. A matte black
surface will return a near 0 value, a highly reflective surface will return values up to 9000.
This results in a 2D image containing distinctions of color and material of objects.
A specific application of the infrared stream is edge detection. When using this application, the
algorithm will specifically look for edges in the infrared image to validate the presence of a certain
object. This detection is mainly used for tooling.

1.3 How does the Arkite Vision sensor work? (Vision license only)

What?
When you are using Arkites Operator Guidance Platform with a Vision licence, the platform is
equipped with an additional high-definition infrared Vision sensor.

How does it work?
The Arkite Vision sensor captures high-quality image and transmits the image data to the Arkite PC.
The Arkite software processes the images and applies different algorithms to them to achieve
accurate and efficient image analysis that can be used for the smart vision features.

About the Arkite software

1.4 Installing the Arkite software

What?
The Arkite software is split in a workstation and a server component. The server component,
containing all data and resources for multiple clients and projects, should preferably run on a separate
windows server to obtain higher security, maintainability and data integrity.

Installation instructions
For instructions on installing the Arkite software, please refer to the Arkite software installation
guide.

1.5 Starting the Arkite software for the first time

What?
The Arkite software automatically starts after the workstation has been turned on. If it does not, you
can double-click the Arkite icon on the desktop.

Connect to the server
When you open the Arkite software for the first time, a welcome wizard appears.
In first screen of this wizard:
  1. In the Server URL or IP field, enter the URL of IP address of the server where the server
    component was installed.
  2. Click Next.
Note
  • If the server component is installed on your workstation, fill in localhost.
  • If the software version on your workstation is not the same as the one on your server, you will
    first need to upgrade. A button will be shown allowing you to download and install the latest
    software version.
About the Arkite software

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Enter your server license key
If your workstation is the first one to connect to the server, you will need to provide a license key in the
next screen of the wizard.

Note
If another workstation already connected to the server before and provided the server license key,
this step wont appear. You will immediately be taken to the next step in the wizard.
To obtain your server license key, click the activation link you have received in an e-mail from Arkite,
fill in the webform and click Submit. If you havent received an activation link, please contact
support@arkite.com.
You will need to provide your Server Id (you can copy this from the information in the screen in the
wizard).
After a few minutes, a license key will be generated and sent to your e-mail. Once you have received
this e-mail:
  1. Copy the license key from the e-mail or download the .key file in attachment of that e-mail and
    save it on the workstation.
  2. In the wizard, paste the license key in the License Key field or click the ... button next to the field
    and select the .key file you have just saved.

  • Between three and two months before your license expires, you will receive a quotation from

    receive a new license key. You can then add this new license key as described above, without

    license key on page 245.

Assign your workstation to a license
In the next step of the wizard, you can assign your workstation to a license, on the condition that a
license key with available slots is present for the server you are connected to. If license keys for
different license types are available, you will be able to choose which license type to use.
Indicate if you want to assign your workstation to a license and click Next.

Note
  • If you have a Vision license, you will only be able to add workstations to it that are Vision
    Ready. If your workstation is not Vision Ready , the option will be disabled. In that case, finish
    the installation without assigning your workstation to a license. Then follow the steps
    described in the procedure How to make your workstation Vision Ready (available on the
    customer drive). The number of workstations you can make Vision Ready is limited to the
    number of workstations for which you have bought a Vision license. If you already have
    reached this number, your request will be denied.
  • If your workstation is Vision Ready , you will not be able to assign it to a Validate or Guide
    license.

  • If no licenses with open slot(s) are available or if you choose to not assign your workstation to
    a license, you can use your workstation as an editor. You will be able to prepare and
    configure projects on them, but you cannot use them to run a project. For testing purposes,
    you will be able to run your project for a maximum of 15 minutes. This way, you can prepare
    your project on your laptop at your desk.

In the next step of the wizard, enter a name for your workstation in the Workstation name field and
click Next. Choose a name that will make it easy for you to identify your workstation.

2. Calibration

2.1 About calibration

Before you can start configuring your project, you will have to calibrate your workstation. Calibration
defines the coordinate system (mm) and origin for all detections.
If you are using the system with Arkite 3D sensor ( Validate or Vision license), both the sensor and
the projector need to be calibrated.
When using a Vision license, you will additionally need to calibrate the Arkite Vision sensor.
During sensor calibration, each XYZ coordinate is translated to a pixel in the sensor image with a
corresponding RGB value.

Projector calibration defines the coordinate system that is used to define where projections need to be
shown on the workbench.
If calibration has not taken place yet on a particular workstation, a popup will appear.

Calibration is one-time operation, but after the calibration the projector and the sensor need to remain
fixed relative to the workbench. When the sensor and/or projector have moved, you have to
recalibrate.

Calibration

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

2.2 Calibrating your workstation

2.2.1 Calibrating a workstation with Arkite 3D sensor using the

calibration wizard (Validate and Vision license only)

What?
The Arkite software contains a calibration wizard that will take you through all the required steps to
calibrate your sensor and projector.

Note
For an optimal result, the scaling settings for your projector in Windows should be configured at
100%. Please verify before you calibrate. In order to do so, right-click in your desktop and select
Display Settings.

Calibration

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Steps
To use the calibration wizard, execute the following steps:
  1. If calibration has not taken place yet on your workstation, click Calibrate in the Calibration info
    popup.
    When recalibrating, click Menu and then Calibration.
Note
When you are in a project, you can also navigate to the Connectivity tab, select the 3D sensor
and select Default Calibration (Sensor+Projector) from the Calibrate menu.

When you have created the project before calibrating, a Projector display is added with the
screen resolution of the device you are working on (e.g. your laptop). This may not match with the
actual projector resolution, used during calibration. This will cause projections to be faulty. You
can fix this by updating the navigating to the Connectivity tab, selecting the Projector card and
updating the Resolution property to the correct value in the Properties pane.
  1. For the initial calibration, select Fully Restart Calibration and click Next.
    To calibrate additional sensors or projectors, use the other options.
  2. Select the 3D Sensor and click Next.
  3. Check the projector settings:
 Verify if the Arkite logo is projected. If not, change the output to which the projector is
connected.

Calibration

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

 Verify if the Arkite logo is projected in the correct orientation on the workbench. Rotate and/or
mirror if required.
 Optionally, check the Enable Height checkbox.
That is useful when you have many detections above the calibration surface, or if your
detections are dynamically updated by an external system.
Note
  • For other use cases, don't enable this setting, since it lowers the calibration accuracy.
  • Currently, the Enable Height option is only available for Optoma ZH420, Optoma ZW400 and
    Optoma ZH403 projectors.
 When finished, click Next.
  1. Make sure the sensor image matches the orientation on the workbench. Apply mirroring if
    required. When finished, click Next.
Calibration

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. Verify whether the four calibration markers are projected correctly on the workbench. Drag them
    into a position where they are on a flat surface (i.e. the table, not a tool or picking bin), as far from
    each other as possible.
  2. Click the center of each marker in the projected image.
    Be as precise as possible. Use the mouse wheel and the right mouse button to zoom and pan.
Tip
If a marker is difficult to see, you may add a piece of paper on that location.

Calibration

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. If calibration was successful, this will be indicated on the screen. Click Next.
Note
In case calibration was not successful, a message will appear indicating the calibration is invalid. If
the calibration is invalid because of one or more calibration marker(s) for which no depth value
could be measured, the respective marker(s) will be indicated by a red circle. Click the Escape
button once or more until you reach the invalid marker. Click the marker(s) again. If that doesnt
work, click Previous to return to the previous step and drag the markers to another location.
  1. Define the origin of your image by dragging it to a meaningful location, e.g. the corner of the
    workbench. Click Next.
Note
With the workstation, you will also receive a small aluminum plate with the Arkite logo. You should
screw the plate onto the workbench at the location where you want define your origin. This will
help you to calibrate, or to re-calibrate in case of issues.

Calibration

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. Verify if the projection on your workbench matches the position on the sensor image. If it does,
    click Finish. If not, click Previous to adjust your calibration.
Result
Your sensor and projector have been calibrated. If you have multiple sensors or projectors, run the
calibration wizard again to calibrate them as well.

2.2.2 Calibrating a workstation with Arkite Vision sensor (Vision

license only)

What?
When you are using the Arkite Operator Guidance Platform with a Vision license, also your Vision
camera will need to be calibrated.

Steps
Follow the steps in the Arkite Vision sensor calibration wizard. When using your workstation for the
first time, the calibration wizard will pop up automatically after you have finished the Arkite 3D sensor
and projector calibration wizard.
If not, you can start the wizard by navigating to the Connectivity tab, select the Arkite Vision Sensor
and select Default Calibration from the Calibrate menu.

To use the calibration wizard, execute the following steps:
  1. Check the projector settings:
    Verify if the Arkite logo is projected. If not, change the output to which the projector is
    connected.
    Verify if the Arkite logo is projected in the correct orientation on the workbench. Rotate and/or
    mirror if required.
 Click Next.
  1. Select the type of lens that is used on your Arkite Vision Sensor and click Next. The lens types
    below are supported:
    8 mm
 12 mm
 16 mm
 25 mm

Calibration

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Note
You can find this information on the lens.
  1. Adjust the brightness of the Arkite Vision sensor:
    Put a typical workpiece under the sensor.
    Rotate the diaphragm ring (=the top ring) of the Vision sensor until the status is green.
 Tighten the screw.
 Click Next.
  1. Take the 5 Arkite Calibration documents you have received with your hardware. Arrange them on
    your workbench so the Siemens stars have a configuration like the one below..
    Rotate the focus ring (=the bottom ring) of the Vision sensor until the image is sharp.
Calibration

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Note
If you dont have the Arkite Calibration documents anymore or if you didnt receive them, you can
download a pdf version from the corresponding step in the Vision calibration wizard in our
software, or from the customer drive.
  1. Verify whether the four calibration markers are projected correctly on the workbench. Drag them
    into a position where they are on a flat surface (i.e. the table, not a tool or picking bin), as far from
    each other as possible.
  2. Verify if the text on the Arkite Calibration document is projected in the correct, readable orientation
    on the workbench. Rotate and/or mirror if required.
  3. Click the center of each marker in the projected image.
  4. Because the Arkite Vision sensor uses infrared, the markers are by default not visible in the
    captured image. Therefore, use the crosshair markers on the Arkite Calibration document and
    align them with the projected markers to make them visible in the captured image.
    Be as precise as possible. Use the mouse wheel and the right mouse button to zoom and pan.
Result
Your Arkite Vision sensor has been calibrated.

3. Projects.........................................................................................................................

3.1 About projects

Projects contain all the information that is required to support your jobs. A job is a work task that an
operator performs on a workstation, for example an assembly, a kitting application, a quality inspection
etc., or any other work task for which you want to guide your operators through augmented reality
work instructions.
Only one project can be loaded at the same time on a workstation. Therefore, make sure to manage
all jobs that the workstation is used for within the same project.
If you have different production lines in which an entirely different set of jobs should be supported, you
can create a different project for each production line.

3.2 Creating a project

What?
When you open the Arkite software for the first time, no projects will be available. The first thing you
need to do is to create a project.

Steps
To create a new project, execute the following steps:
  1. On the Projects tab, click New Project.
  2. In the Properties pane, update the project properties:
    In the Name field, provide an appropriate name for your project.
    Note
    Next to the Name label, the object ID for the project is shown. You can copy it to use it when
    working with the Arkite API. For more information about the Arkite API, refer to chapter 18 The
    Arkite API on page 281.
    By clicking the Comment icon next to the Name property, you can provide a short explanation
    of the purpose of the project.
    Note
    If you want to load the project automatically when starting the Arkite software as a run-only user,
    check the Auto open on this workstation on startup checkbox.
Projects

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

This checkbox is only available for projects that have a production version, since projects that only
have a Draft version are only available to Admin users.

Result
Your project is added to the project list and you are ready to go. To start configuring your project, click
the 0.1 Draft button next to the project name or right-click the project and select Open.

Note
In case of issues with your project, for example a communication loop, you can open your project
without running it to troubleshoot. To do so, right-click the project and select Open without
running.

3.3 Managing projects

What?
You can find an overview of all projects that are available on your workstation in the Projects menu.
Only one project can be loaded on the workstation at the same time. That project is rendered in bold.

When you are working in a project, you can always return to your project overview by clicking the
Menu button.

Projects

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

To return to your project, close the Menu.

How to manage projects
On the Projects tab, you can:

 Click Import to import a project prepared on another server
 Select a project and click Export to make it available for use on another server.

 Select a project and click Export to Arkite to provide a copy to Arkite for support.
 Right-click a project and select Duplicate to duplicate it.

 Right-click a project and select Delete or click the button in the project row to delete it.

3.4 Versioning

3.4.1 About versioning........................................................................................

What?
Every project has a specific version and status at all times. The current version and status of a project
is shown next to each project in the project overview as well as in the Properties pane.

Project versions
A projects version consists of a major and a minor version number.
Every time a new version is created, the minor version number increases with one digit, e.g. from 0.1
to 0.2.
When the project status is changed to Production , the major version number increases with one digit
and the minor version number is reset to 0, e.g. from 0.4 to 1.0.

Projects

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Project workflows
The Arkite software supports different project workflows:

 The most simple workflow only discriminates between projects that are still being configured and
projects that are being used in production. Once the project has been finalized, the project status
is changed from Draft to Production.

 In a more advanced setup, a Review status is added to the workflow. In this status, the project is
validated on all workstations before it is being put into Production.

 In the most advanced workflow, a project needs to be approved by one or more approvers before
it can be used in production.

Note
For more information on how to define which workflow is implemented, refer to section 3.4.2
Versioning settings on page 35.

Project statuses
A project can have the statuses in the table below. Depending on the project workflow that is
implemented, one or more statuses can be skipped.

Status Description

Draft The project is being prepared offsite.

Review The project is being validated on all workstations.
Production The project is ready to be used in production.

Production  Awaiting approval The project is ready to be used in production, but still needs to be
approved by one or more approvers.
Production  Approved The project is ready to be used in production and has been
approved by all required approvers.

Projects

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Status Description

Production  Rejected The project was ready to be used in production but was rejected by
at least one approver.

Note
  • In the workflows in which the Review status is used, only projects with status Draft can be
    edited or removed.
  • In the Draft-Production workflow, the Admin user can still edit a project in status Production
    as long as no new Draft version has been created.
    A project needs to be in status Production Approved in order to be used in production. Operators
    (i.e. users without permissions to create or manage projects in the Arkite software) will only be able to
    open and run projects in status Production Approved.
    As an example, consider a case in which four projects are available:
    a project in status Draft (version 0.1)
    a project in status Review (version 0.2)
    a project in status Production Approved (version 1.0)
 a project for which a production version exists, but is currently being updated (status Draft ,
version 1.1)
Users with admin permissions will be able to see and open all projects. For the project with version
1.1, he can choose to open the production version or the current draft version.

Operators can only open the production version of a project. Draft and review versions of a project are
not clickable.

Projects

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  3. Under Versioning , select the workflow you want to be used:
 If you only want to use the statuses Draft and Production, select the Draft  Production radio
button.
 If you want to use the status Review too, select the Draft  Review  Production radio
button.
  1. In case you want one or more users to approve a project before it is used in production:
    Check the Approval required for status change to Production checkbox.
    Click the Add button and select the role of the user that needs to approve the project.
 To define multiple approvers with different roles, add all the required roles.
 To define multiple approvers with the same role, change the number of approvers in the
Number of Approvals column.

Projects

3.4.4 Approving or rejecting a project

What?
In case the project workflow with approval is configured, one or more users with a role which has the
Approve Projects permission need to log in to the Arkite software and approve the project, before it
can be used in production.

Projects

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

How to approve a project
To approve a project, execute the steps below:
  1. Log in to the Arkite software with a user that has a role with the Approve Projects permission. By
    default, the Approver role has this permission.
  2. Select the project with status Production Waiting for Approval.
  3. In the Properties pane under Version and status , click Approve / Reject.
The Project Approval Decisions window appears.
  1. To approve the project, click Approve.
The Electronic Signature window appears.
  1. Enter your password and, optionally, a comment.
    Note
    You can click the button to make the password youve entered visible and verify if you havent
    made any typing mistakes.
  2. Check the The project has been validated on all workstations checkbox.
  3. Click the Approve button.
Projects

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

The approval is registered.
If you were the only or the last approver, the status is changed to Production  Approved.

If more approvals are required, the status remains in Production  Waiting for Approval.

How to reject a project
To reject a project, execute the steps below:
  1. Log in to the Arkite software with a user that has a role with the Approve Projects permission. By
    default, the Approver role has this permission.
  2. Select the project with status Production Waiting for Approval.
  3. In the Properties pane under Version and status , click Approve / Reject.
The Project Approval Decisions window appears.
  1. To reject the project, click Reject.
The Electronic Signature window appears.
  1. Enter your password and a reason for the rejection in the Comment field.
    Note
    You can click the button to make the password youve entered visible and verify if you havent
    made any typing mistakes.
  2. Click the Reject button.
Projects

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

The rejection is registered.
The status is changed to Production  Rejected.
Any additional approvers will no longer be able to approve the project at this stage.

Note
It is also possible to approve or reject a project from the projects version history:
  • Select the project you want to approve or reject.
  • In the Properties pane under Status , click Versions.
  • In the Approval column, click the text Awaiting approval.
  • Approve or reject the project as explained in the section above.

3.5 Working on projects with multiple authors

What?
In your project overview, you have access to all projects on any workstation connected to the same
server. This also allows you to work on the same project with multiple authors, and to use the same
project on multiple workstations. If for example the same or a very similar assembly process is taking
place on several workstations, the project will be stored on the server and can be edited and
maintained from different workstation.

Projects

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Opening a project created on another workstation
In your Projects overview under the Menu , you will see all projects that are on the server, also the
ones that were created on another workstation.
When opening a project for the first time on your workstation, the complete project is copied from
another workstation, including all workstation specific settings and properties such as visualizations
and the location of detections. The popup below will appear when opening the workstation. Select the
workstation you want to copy from and click OK.

Note
If you want to open the project on an editor, i.e. a workstation without a license, the system will by
default switch to another workstation. If you want to open the project on the editor, you first need
to add the editor to the workstations in the project properties:
  • Select the project
  • In the Properties pane under Workstations , click the Add button.
  • Select a workstation to copy from and click OK.
Projects

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Editing a project created on another workstation
From that moment, you can start editing the project yourself. Anything you add or change, will also be
immediately available on the other workstation.
Note
If the project is being edited on several workstations simultaneously, its possible the project is
changed on another workstation before your change can be applied. In that case, the pop up
below will appear. Your change will be reverted, the project will be restarted.

Global properties versus workstation-specific properties
Some properties and settings are global. This means they are valid for the project as such and are
always exactly the same on each workstation. This applies for example for detections. If you add a
detection, change its name or delete it, this will have an immediate effect on all other workstations.
Some properties and settings are workstation specific. This means they can be different on every
workstation. This applies for example for the location of a detection. If you add a detection and teach
it, the detection and its location is copied on all other workstations. However, if you change the
location afterwards, e.g. by reteaching it, the location will only change on that particular workstation.
In the user interface, its always indicated if something is global or local/workstation specific.
For example, the location of visualizations on a Projector display is local or workstation specific, as
you can see on the screenshot below.

Projects

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

The location of visualizations on a Screen display is global however, as you can see on the
screenshot below.

Some elements have properties that are global and others that are local. In the screenshot below, you
can see this for an Inter-Workstation communication module:

The table below gives an overview of the most important global and workstation specific aspects of a
project:

Global Local / Workstation specific

Project name, description and status Location of a detection ( Validate license only)

Processes Display Port
Process steps Value of a non-shared variable

Text and image instructions
Displays
Location of visualizations on a Screen display

Variables
Value of a shared variable

Sharing variables
For manual variables and communication variables, you have the choice to synchronize the value
across different workstations or to manage them independently. In order to synchronize values for a
variable, check the Shared checkbox in the Variables window.
You can share variables while running the same project on different workstations, but you can also
share variables across projects.
In the example below, two variables have been created, one shared variable and one unshared
variable. They both have the value Workstation 1.
Be aware that:
 If youre working in the same project, creating the variables on one workstation will also create
them on the other workstations.

 If youre working in different projects, you need to create the variables in both projects on both
stations, and mark them as shared accordingly.

Projects

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Then, the value of both variables is updated to Workstation 2 on one of the workstations.

On the other workstations, the value of the shared variable is updated to Workstation 2 as well. The
value of the unshared variable hasnt changed however: it is still Workstation 1.

3.6 Switching workstations

What?
When you are working on an editor, i.e. a workstation that has not been assigned to a license, you can
switch to another workstation on the same server. From then, your editor will impersonate that
workstation: all workstation specific properties from that workstation will be loaded, and all local
properties you edit will be changed on that workstation and that workstation only. Also the license of
that workstation will be used.

How to switch workstations
In the top bar, click your workstation name and select Switch Workstation.

Projects

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

In the Select a Workstation window, select the workstation of your choice and click OK.

Note
If a project is open when you are switching workstations, the project will be closed after switching.
You need to re-open it.

Automatic switch of workstation when opening a project
When you are working on an editor and open a project that has never been opened on that editor
before, the system will automatically switch to another workstation.
The Switch to Workstation pop-up will appear. Select the workstation you want to switch to and click
OK.

Note
If you want to open the project on your editor instead of switching to another workstation, you first
need to add the editor to the workstations in the project properties:
  • Select the project
  • In the Properties pane under Workstations , click the Add button.
  • In the Select a Workstation window, select the workstation you want to add to the project and
    click OK.
Projects

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

By default, your own workstation is selected.
  • Select a workstation to copy from and click OK.
Jobs

4. Jobs

4.1 About jobs and job steps

Jobs
A job is a work task that an operator performs on a workstation, for example an assembly, a kitting
application, a quality inspection etc., or any other work task for which you want to guide your operators
through augmented reality work instructions.

Steps
A job will consist of different steps, some of which can be optional, based on one or more properties of
the product to assemble.

Job Options
Job options allow you to define different properties for which the assembly steps in your job assembly
can be slightly different.
Example
Suppose youre assembling a particular car model. Some options for the job assembly could be:
  • The fuel type : petrol, diesel, electric, ...
  • The transmission : manual, automatic, ...
  • The color : blue, black, red, ...
Job Variants
The combination of different job options results in different job variants.

Example
Suppose youre assembling a particular car model with options color, fuel type and transmission.
Some variants for the job assembly could be:
  • a blue car with manual transmission that rides on diesel.
  • a black car with automatic transmission that rides on petrol.
Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

4.3 Configuring steps

About configuring steps
A job will consist of different steps, some of which can be optional, based on one or more properties of
the product to assemble.
On the Steps tab, you can define all the steps in your job assembly.

To add a new step, execute the steps below:
  1. Navigate to the Steps tab.
  2. In the ribbon, select the job for you which you want to add steps.

4.3.2 Setting up your step structure

About setting up your step structure
Several possibilities are available to apply a structure your assembly steps, with the purpose of
creating a better overview for your operators, manage step order or repetition or mark steps as
optional.
The sections below provide more information about each of the possibilities below:
 Numbered steps
 Composite steps
 The Switch Job Option step

 The Switch step
 The Check Quality step with rework flows

Numbered steps
A numbered step is a logical step in your job assembly from the viewpoint of the operator. It can
consist of multiple (detection) steps in the Arkite software.
Example
The operator step Fix a screw can consist of the detection steps below:
  • Take screwdriver
  • Pick screw
  • Tighten screw
  • Place screwdriver
    Using numbered steps, you can add structure to your job assembly and divide it into different
    subassemblies. You can create different levels of numbered steps.
    Example
    In our demo fuel filter assembly job, the subassembly where the cap is assembled onto the fuel
    filter housing could be assembled like this:
Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

1. Assemble cap
1.1. Place the cap
Pick cap
Place cap
1.2. Fix the cap
Take screwdriver
Pick screw
Tighten screw
Place screwdriver
The numbered steps in your job assembly can be displayed on the operator screen using a
Numbered Steps List visualization. It serves as a table of contents, intended to help the operator in
gaining insight into the assembly process. The Arkite project template contains a preconfigured
Numbered Steps List , but you can also add and configure one yourself. For more information, refer
to section Numbered Steps List on page 99.

Composite steps
A composite step is a step that consists of two or more child steps. These child steps can be individual
steps or other composite steps, that in their turn also consist of child steps.
In the Properties pane for a composite step, you can define in which order and how often the child
steps need to be executed.

Property Description

Name The name for the process step.
Note
Next to the Name label, the object ID for the process step is shown. You
can copy it to use it when working with the Arkite API.

Child step order Define in which order the child steps are executed:
 Sequential order ( icon):
The child steps are executed in the order in which they appear. This is the
default option.
 Any order ( icon - Validate and Vision licenses only):
It does not matter in which order the child steps are executed. However, all
child steps must be executed for the process to continue to the next step.
 One arbitrary step ( icon):
Only one of the child steps should be executed for the process to continue
to the next step.
 All steps simultaneously ( icon - Validate and Vision licenses
only):
All steps should be executed at exactly the same time for the process to
continue to the next step. For example, you can use this type of step to
check if all tools are present when you start the assembly, or if you want
an operator to press two virtual buttons at the same time to confirm an
action, as a safety measure.
Note
Do not use the Any order and All steps simultaneously options when
using a Guide license, because in that case there is no way to verify
which child steps are executed by the operator. When running a project
that contains such steps on a system without sensor, these steps will be
treated by the system as sequential steps.

Child step instruction separator Only available if the Child step order^ is Any order , One arbitrary step^ or
All steps simultaneously.

Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Property Description
Define which separator word should be used to concatenate the instructions
for the different child steps:
 Auto:
Use the default separator. For Any order and All steps simultaneously ,
the default is and. For One arbitrary step , the default is or.
 And:
Use and as a separator.
 Or:
Use or as a separator.
Example
If you have a composite step, configured as Any Order with two child
steps Take Screwdriver and Pick Screw , by default the system will
show the instruction Take Screwdriver and Pick Screw.
Note
Instead of concatenating the instructions for the different child steps, you
can also define a custom instruction on the level of the composite step.

Repetition Indicate if the composite step should be repeated:
 None:
The composite step is executed only once. After execution of the last child
step, the process continues with the step after the composite step.
 Repeat:
The step is repeated in an endless loop. After the execution of the last
child step, the first child step is executed again.
Note
This feature should be used in combination with a condition: the
composite step is repeated as long as the condition is valid. For more
information about working with conditions, refer to section 6.7 Working
with conditions on page 177.
 Repeat number of times:
The step is repeated a specified number of times (see below).
 Repeat for each element:
The step is repeated for all elements in a specified list (see below).
Number of repetitions If you have indicated the step should be repeated for a specified number of
times, enter the number of repetitions in this field.
You can also specify a variable that contains the number of repetitions. To do
so, click the icon and select the variable containing the number of
repetitions. Alternatively, you can also type the variable name between
double braces, i.e. {{Variable name}}.
List of elements to loop over If you have indicated the step should be repeated for all elements in a
specified list, enter the list here.
You can also specify a variable that contains the list. To do so, click the
icon and select the variable containing the list. Alternatively, you can also
type the variable name between double braces, i.e. {{Variable name}}.

List type If you have indicated the step should be repeated for all elements in a
specified list, enter the list type here:
 Json Array
 List with separator

Separator If you have indicated the step should be repeated for all elements in a
specified list of type List with separator , enter the separator here.

Variable for current element If you have indicated the step should be repeated for all elements in a
specified list, this variable will be updated with the current element.
Variable for count If you have indicated the step should be repeated for all elements in a
specified list, this variable will be updated with the total number of elements
in the list.

Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Property Description

Variable for index If you have indicated the step should be repeated for a specified number of
times or for all elements in a specified list, this variable will be updated with
the current iteration.

The Switch Job Option step
The Switch Job Option step allows you to set up different assembly flows for the different values of a
job option.

Property Description

Name The^ name for the Switch^ Job Option^ step.^ By clicking the Comment^ icon
next to the Name property, you can add a few words of explanation
regarding the use of the step.
Note
Next to the Name label, the object ID for the process step is shown. You
can copy it to use it when working with the Arkite API.

Job Option Select the job option for which you want to create different assemblies.

Switch Cases By default, a case will be available for every possible value of the job option.
In your steps tree, there will be a branch for each value. Under each branch
you can add the required steps for that value.
In case more values require exactly the same actions, you can group these
values by dragging them into the same case. Doing so will also merge the
branches in the steps tree.
If you want to undo the merging of a case, you can right-click one of the
values and click Move to New Case.

Example
Suppose youre assembling a particular car model. One job option could be the cars fuel type
(petrol, diesel, electric).
The Switch Job Option step allows you to easily set up specific steps for each fuel type.
The screenshot below show the default configuration, with a separate branch for each fuel type.

The Switch step
The Switch step allows you to set up different cases with substeps. Only one of the cases will be
executed, depending on the value of the variable you assigned to the switch.
To set up a switch, configure the properties below:

Property Description

Name The^ name for the Switch^ step.^ By clicking the Comment^ icon next to the
Name property, you can add a few words of explanation regarding the use of
the step.
Note
Next to the Name label, the object ID for the process step is shown. You
can copy it to use it when working with the Arkite API.

Variable for Switch The state of this variable will determine which case will be executed.

Switch Cases Enter the value(s) for which you want to execute different substeps. Type a
value and press the Enter button to submit it. You can add multiple values
for one case. By default, two cases are available, but you can add more
cases by clicking the button or remove cases by selecting them and
clicking the button.
Example
In the example below, three cases are defined based on the value of the
Torque Result variable. Different steps will be executed if the value is
either Within Tolerance , Too High or Too Low.

Property Description

Add Default Case Check this property to add a case to execute for any value of the Switch^
Variable that is not assigned to another case.

For each of the cases, a subpath is created within the Switch step. In each of these subpaths, you
can add steps defining what needs to be done in the situation at hand.

The Check Quality step with rework flows (Vision license only)

Rework Flow substeps are automatically created for each possible class linked to the quality check
detection.
By default, the three classes below are linked to an object with quality check detection :

 The Without class
 The Expected Result class

 The Bad Result class

 The Expected Result class

Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

 The Bad Result class
 The Missing class

Note
In the Properties of the quality detection or the object with quality check detection, you can add
more classes or rename existing classes. Under Quality Check Classes , click the button and
provide a name and a type for your class. A new class is typically created if you want to show a
different error text or give different rework instructions.
In the example below, two classes have been created for specific WRONG situations, and the
class with MISSING type has been renamed to match the specific situation.

For each Rework Flow substep, you can:
 add process steps defining what needs to be done in the situation at hand
 for Quality Check Classes of type WRONG or MISSING: define an error message in the
Properties of the Rework Flow step.

When the Check Quality step is triggered, the corresponding Quality or Object with Quality Check
detection will be evaluated. Depending on the result of this evaluation, the corresponding rework flow
will be selected. The process steps in this path will be activated and in case of a result of type
WRONG or MISSING, the error message you have defined will be displayed in red on both the
Projector and the Screen.

Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

In the example below:
 For each of the classes, the status of a variable will be logged.
 In case of a result of type Missing or Wrong , the number of the errors will be counted and specific
detections with customized instructions will be triggered

What happens after the execution of the rework flow, depends on the initial evaluation of the quality
check:

 If the evaluation resulted in a class of type CORRECT, the system will execute the steps in the
rework flow and then move to the next step in the process.
 If the evaluation resulted in a class of type WRONG or MISSING, the system will execute the
steps in the corresponding rework flow and then re-evaluate the Quality detection. That process
will continue until the Expected Result is reached.

You can organize your steps as described below:
 Right-click a step and select Duplicate to duplicate it.
 Select a process step and drag it with your mouse to change its order.
 To delete a process step, you can:
 Select it and press the Delete key on your keyboard

 Right-click the step and select Delete.
 Right-click a step, select Move and then To job to move the step to another job.
Select the job you want to move the step to and click OK.
 Right-click a step, select Move and then To process to move the step to a process.
Select the process you want to move the step to and click OK.

4.3.3 Step types

This section contains an overview of all types of steps that are available to you to build your job
assembly. They are divided in the categories below:
 General steps : some basic, often used steps.
 Variables : steps that use the values of a variable as an input or an output.

 Detections : steps related to the detections you have added
 Materials: steps related to the materials you have configured.
 Screen buttons: steps related to the buttons you have added to the touch screen.
 Communication: steps related to the communication modules you have configured.

 Extra : a number of advanced, less often used steps.

General steps
The table below gives an overview of all process step types that are available in the General steps
subtab:

Step type Description

Numbered step A logical step in your job assembly from the viewpoint of the operator. It can
consist of multiple (detection) steps. The numbered steps in your job assembly
can be displayed on the operator screen using a Numbered Steps List
visualization. It serves as a table of contents, intended to help the operator in
gaining insight into the assembly process.
Note
For more information, refer to section Numbered steps on page 57.

Composite step A step that can contain a number of child^ steps. It allows you to control the order
in which child steps need to be executed or to repeat the child steps a number o
times.
Note
For more information, refer to section Composite steps on page 58.

Delay Set a certain time in milliseconds for the job to wait.

Execute task A number of steps coming from a task. Tasks allow you to re-use the same steps
across jobs.
Note
For more information, refer to section 6.8 Working with tasks on page 177.

Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Step type Description

Job Control Go to a specific step in your job.
You can either select the step or type the name of the step in a field.
Note
If the field contains a value that does not match with a step name, the Job
Control step will not be executed and an error will be added in the error tray.
If the field contains the name of the Job Control step itself, the Job Control
step will not be executed.
If the field contains a value that matches with multiple step names, the first
step with a matching step name will be activated.
When using the step in a process, you can also choose to:
 Go to the next step in the active job
 Go to the previous step in the active job, on the condition this previous step is
either a detection step or a work instruction.

Operator Dialog Show a popup on the operator screen, asking the operator to confirm an action
or to make a choice. The operators choice is saved in a response variable.
Combine this step with a Switch step using the response variable.

Process Control Control a particular process. You can either select the process or type the name
of the process in a field.
Note
If the field contains a value that does not match with a process name, the
Process Control step will not be executed and an error will be added in the
error tray.
You can choose to:
 Reset a process
 Pause a process
 Pause and reset a process
 Start a (paused) process  the process will continue from the step where it has
been paused
 Restart a process, i.e. reset and start it
 Go to the next step in a process
 Go to the previous step in a process
Note
Going to a Previous step is only possible if that previous is step is a detection
step or work instruction.
 Go to a specific step in a process. You can either select the step or type the
name of the step in a field.
Note
If the field contains a value that does not match with a step name, the
Process Control step will not be executed and an error will be added in the
error tray.
If the field contains the name of the Process Control step itself, the Process
Control step will not be executed.
If the field contains a value that matches with multiple step names, the first
step with a matching step name will be activated.

Resetter Reset a variable or entity to its default state.

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Step type Description

Snapshot Takes a snapshot from the selected feed and stores it as a *.jpeg or a Data URI.
Note
For making RGB product snapshots, we recommend using a Daheng RGB
sensor. When connecting a Daheng RGB sensor, the exposure time is set by
default to 30 milliseconds.
To set another exposure time, navigate to the Connectivity tab and select
the sensor card. In the Properties pane under Exposure , uncheck the
Automatic checkbox and in the Exposure time (ms) property, set the
exposure time of your choice.

Switch Job Option Step that allows you to set up different assembly flows, for the different values of

60.

you assigned to the switch.
Note
For more information, refer to section The Switch step on page 61.

Work Instruction Provide additional text and/or image instructions.
Note
The process will never automatically continue after a Work Instruction step,
Therefore you always need to provide a Next or Confirm button on the
screen or combine it with a Job Control step.

Variables
The table below gives an overview of all process step types that are available in the Variables subtab:

Step type Description

Counter Increment or decrement the value of a variable by 1

Find and Replace String Allows you to look for a text string within a fixed or dynamic text and replace it
with another text string.
Example
Suppose you want to flatten a multi-line Windows-style string into a single
line, separating the original lines with a |.
Add a Find and Replace String step with the configuration below:
Input: (the variable containing) the original multi-line string
Find string: \r \n
Replace string: |
Variable for result: typically the same variable that contained the original
multi-line string, but you could also select another variable.

Function Allows you to calculate or evaluate a function with fixed numbers and/or dynamic
content based on the value of one or more variables.
For a full overview of the supported functions, please consult the framework
documentation.
Note
Always use. as the decimal separator to separate the integer part from the
fractional part of a number.
To define the order of several operations, brackets () can be used.

Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Step type Description

Set Variable Update the value of a variable or a list of variables.
In the State to Set field, enter the value you want to set for the selected
variable(s). To insert dynamic content, click the icon at the location where
you want to include the content and select the variable containing the dynamic
content. Alternatively, you can also type the variable name between double
braces, i.e. {{Variable name}}. You can also use a variable within a variable.

The variable you want to update can also be dynamic: by selecting the By Name
option you can provide a variable name with fixed and dynamic parts.
This allows you to update variables in a loop. To do so, embed the step in a
composite step that is repeated for a number of elements.
Example
If you provide the name Orientation_x{{index}} , the variable that is set will
depend on the value of the index variable. If the value of the index variable is
01 at the time of execution of the step, the variable Orientation_x01 will be
set.

Split String by Index Extracts a fragment of a string in a variable based on:
 index: the position of the first character of the string
 length: the number of characters to extract, starting from the index
Split String by Argument Extracts a fragment of a string in a variable based on:
 split symbol: a character used to split the string
 index: the number of occurrences of the split symbol after which you want to
extract the fragment
Use the Variable property for the string that needs to be split, the Variable for
Result property for the extracted fragment and the Variable for remainder
property for what is left of the string after extracting the fragment you needed.
Example
If the string you want to split is
Arkite;is;a;great;system;for;guiding;operators and you want to retain
only the word great , then you can use ; as a split symbol and 4 as index.
In that case, the variable indicated in the Variable for remainder property will
contain what is left from the string, i.e.
Arkite;is;a;system;for;guiding;operators

String Formatter Compiles a text string containing fixed text and/or dynamic text based on the
value of one or more variables. To insert dynamic text, click the icon at the
location where you want to include the text and select the variable containing the
dynamic text. Alternatively, you can also type the variable name between double
braces, i.e. {{Variable name}}. You can also use a variable within a variable. For
example, if the value of a variable Index is 01, then {{Variable{{Index}}}} will
resolve into the value of the variable Variable01.
Tip
For long text strings, click the icon to enlarge the String to format text
box.

String Parser Searches a JSON or XML string for the names of specified variables and stores
the corresponding values of the first match as the current state of those
variables.
Variable changed Check the value of a particular variable.
Depending on the specific settings, the job will continue if:
 the variable has a particular value
 the variable does not have a particular value
 the variables value matches another variables value
 the variables value does not match another variables value
 the variables value is changed

Variable Logger Log the current state of one or more variables.

Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Detections
At a certain point in your assembly, you can integrate a step in which an action is done with a
detection.
However, before you can do so, you first need to add the detection:
 Click the New Job Detection button in the Detections subtab to add a detection you only want to
use in the job you are configuring.
 Click the New Project-Wide Detection button in the Detections subtab to add a detection you
want to use in all the jobs in your project.

For more information regarding the next steps, refer to section 5.5 Adding detections on page 121.

Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

You can also add a step in which the detection that is used depends on the value of a variable.

In the popup that appears, select a detection type and action, and specify a variable in the Variable
for detection name property. If this variable contains a value that does not match with a detection in
the project, or with a detection that is not taught, the project will be paused. An error will be shown in
the error tray and logged in the variable configured in the Variable for error message property.

The actions that are available to be used in a process step depend on the detection type. The table
below provides you with an overview of available actions per detection type.

Detection type Available actions

Object  Place: put the object at the location where it should be.
 Take: remove the object from the location where it should be.

Tool (^) Place: put the tool at the location where it should be.
Take: remove the tool from the location where it should be.

Detection type Available actions

Picking bin  Place bin: put the picking bin at the location where it should be.
 Take bin: remove the picking bin from the location where it should be.
 Pick: take material from the picking bin
Note
If you are adding a pick step, it is often better to use the material from the
Materials subtab, rather than the picking bin. If at some point, the material is
linked to a different picking bin, your pick step will be automatically updated.

Quality step with rework flows (Vision license only) on page 62.

Note
When a detection is not taught, the step cannot be completed: the action that is required to trigger
the detection is not available. If teaching the detection is not possible (when using the system with
a Guide license), you always need to provide a Next or Confirm button on the screen or combine
it with a Job Control step.

Materials
At a certain point in your assembly, you can integrate a step in which a material is picked from a
picking bin.
However, before you can do so, you first need to add the material. Click the Add Material button in
the Materials subtab.

For more information regarding the next steps, refer to section 5.8 Managing materials on page 151.
In the Number of Items property, you can indicate how many pieces need to be picked from the
picking bin. If this property contains a value that is more than one, the number of items will
automatically be appended to the text instruction that is displayed to the operator.

Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Note
Be aware the sensor cannot see or verify if the correct number of items is actually picked from the
picking bin. It will just validate the picking action itself.
You can also add a step in which the material that is picked depends on the value of a variable,
defined in the Variable for material name property. If this variable contains a value that does not
match with a material in the project, contains a material that is not linked to a picking bin or is linked to
a picking bin that is not taught, the project will be paused. An error will be shown in the error tray and
logged in the variable configured in the Variable for error message property.

Note
When there is no picking bin defined for the material, or if the defined picking bin is not taught, the
step cannot be completed: the action that is required to trigger the detection is not available. If
teaching the picking bin is not possible (when using the system with a Guide license), you always
need to provide a Next or Confirm button on the screen or combine it with a Job Control step.

Screen buttons
At a certain point in your assembly, you can integrate a step in which a screen button on the touch
screen is pressed.
However, before you can do so, you first need to add the button on a Screen display. Until you have
done this, the Screen buttons subtab in the overview of process steps will be empty.
For more information, refer to section 4.4.3 Adding visualizations on page 100.

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

However, before you can do so, you first need to configure a communication module. Click the New
Communication button in the Communication subtab and select a module of your choice.

4.3.4 Testing your job

You can test your job by selecting the job variant or the job option values of your choice in the ribbon
and then clicking the Test Job button.

The icons for every step indicate the progress of your job:

Icon Description

The step has not been started yet.

The step is currently active (Run mode).
For composite steps, the part of the circle that is filled indicates the percentage of the
child steps that is executed.

The step is currently active, but is suspended because the project is not running (Edit
mode).
For composite steps, the part of the circle that is filled indicates the percentage of the
child steps that is executed.

The step has been completed.

The step will be ignored due to variant and condition logic.

Depending on the step type, the icon can be circular, square or triangular:

Icon Description

The step is linked to a trigger. The job will continue to the next step after the trigger has
been completed.
Examples of such steps are Detection, Material or Wait for Communication steps.

The step will complete instantly. The job will continue to the next step immediately.^
You cant associate any visualizations with this step, because they would never be
displayed anyway.
Examples of such steps are Set Variable or Send Communication steps.

Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Icon Description

The step is blocking the process ^ in its current state, the job will never continue to the
next step.
This can have several causes:
 A detection is not taught ( Detection step)
 A detection is disabled ( Detection step)
 There is no picking bin defined for a material ( Material step)
 There is no picking bin taught for a material ( Material step)
 There is no trigger defined for the step ( Work Instruction step)

Note
On an editor, i.e. a workstation without a valid Guide , Validate or Vision license, you will be able
to run a project for a maximum of 15 minutes. After that, it will automatically revert to Edit mode.
To force the job to go to the next step, click the Next button.
To return to the previous step, click the Previous button. Going to a Previous step is only possible if
that previous is step is a detection step or work instruction.
To go to a specific step, select the step and click the Go To button.
To reset the job and start again from the beginning, click the Reset Job button in the ribbon.

4.3.5 Job selection and job execution

The Operator Job Selection process
When you create a project, on the Processes tab, by default one process called Operator Job
Selection will be available that is started when the project is loaded.
The Operator job selection process consists of three major steps in which an operator:

 Selects a job from a gallery on the touch screen
 Selects a variant from a gallery on the touch screen
 Enters a quantity on the touch screen

After the selection, the selected job variant is executed the specified number of times. After the last
iteration, the job selection is automatically started again.
When you add new jobs or new job variants, these are automatically added to the galleries on the
selection screens.
Warning
If you havent configured any job variants, the job will be executed skipping all optional steps (if
there are any).

Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

With the Generate menu, you can add a job selection process yourself.

For more information, refer to section 6.2 Generating Job Selection processes on page 164.

The Job Screen Template
While a job is being executed, a screen with the information below is displayed:

 A menu bar allowing you to switch languages, experience level or users, to turn your projectors on
and off, to shut down the system or to restart the project.
 A Numbered Steps List , providing the operator insight into the assembly process
 Information about the current job, such as selected variant, quantity, cycle time and expected
cycle time.
Of course, you can add additional information if needed. Click Edit Job Master to do so.

4.4 Managing visualizations for your job steps

What?
After creating your job steps, you can manage the visualizations that will be displayed when those
steps are active, on a connected projector or screen.
You will see a subtab for every display that is available. By default, a Projector subtab will always be
available.

Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Note
  • When you have created the project before calibrating, a Projector display is added with the
    screen resolution of the device you are working on (e.g. your laptop). This may not match with
    the actual projector resolution, used during calibration. This will cause projections to be faulty.
    A message on the Projector subtab will warn you for this. Click Fix and update the
    Resolution property to the correct value in the projectors Properties pane.
  • To add more displays, refer to section 7.2.3 Adding a display on page 186.
    When creating a process, the Arkite software will automatically generate visualizations to display text
    and image instructions.
    Additionally, you may also create more visualizations to display.
    When the Experience Level functionality is enabled, you can add experience level buttons to a
    Screen display to allow an operator to select his experience level.

4.4.1 Visualization types

Following types of visualizations are available in the Arkite software:
 Draw shape:
A geometrical figure. It can be a (rounded) rectangle, an ellipse, a line, a polygon or an arrow.
 Text:
Visualization that allows you display a text to the user. The text can contain both fixed and
dynamic parts, based on the value of a variable.
 Image:
Visualization that allows you to display a fixed or dynamic image or video to the user.
 Screen button:
Adds a clickable/pressable button to a Screen display. Allows the user to set a variable and/or
control a process or job in your project by doing so.
 Progress bar:
Visualization that shows the progress of a process, or a progress bar based on the state of two
variables.

 Operator Input:
Visualization that allows you to add an input field to a Screen display, in which the operator can
type information. The information is stored in a variable.
 Keyboard:
Visualization that displays an on-screen keyboard onto a Screen display. The operator can use it
to enter information in an Operator Input visualization if no physical keyboard is available.
 Sensor stream (Validate and Vision license only):
Visualization that displays a specific set of detections with their current state.

 Gallery:

Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Visualization that displays a number of tiles with text and images in a grid view on a Screen
display. Operators can tap a tile to select it, and depending on the selection you can store data in
a variable.
 Combo Box:
Visualization that displays a dropdown list with a number of text items on a Screen display.
Operators can select an item from the list, and depending on the selection you can store data in a
variable.
 Table:
Visualization that displays a table with customizable rows and columns on a Screen display.
Optionally, operators can select a row in the table, and depending on the selection you can store
data in a variable.
 Status Bar:
Shows the operator an error message when there is an issue with a communication module, with
a sensor, screen or projector, or when the server is offline.
Note
A status bar is added by default to the bottom of every Screen display. Its location and look and
feel can be edited, and it can also be deleted if not required.

 Menu Bar:
Visualization with preconfigured features for the operator:
 Turn projector(s) on or off (if an IP address for the projector has been configured)
 Restart the project
 Shut down the system
 Change the experience level (if experience level is enabled)

 Change the instruction language (if multiple languages are added to the project)
 Switch the user
By default, an Arkite project contains a Menu Bar on the Screen display already.

 Numbered Steps List:
Visualization that displays the numbered steps from a job that is being executed on a Screen
display. The step that is currently active is highlighted. It serves as a table of contents, intended to
help the operator in gaining insight into the assembly process. The Arkite project template
contains a preconfigured Numbered Steps List , but you can also add and configure one yourself.

Name property
The Name property allows you to define a specific name for the visualization. By clicking the

Note
Next to the Name label, the object ID for the visualization is shown. You can copy it to use it when
working with the Arkite API. For more information about the Arkite API, refer to chapter 18 The
Arkite API on page 281.

Visibility properties
For each visualization, the properties in the table below can be configured in the Visibility section:

Property Description

Visibility Select one of the options below from the Visibility dropdown list:
 On : the visualization will always be visible
 Blink : the visualization will blink. Use the Blink Interval property to define how
fast the visualization will blink.
 Based on Variable : the visibility of the visualization will be based on the current
state of the variable provided in the Variable for visibility property.

Variable for visibility Only available if the Based on Variable option is selected in the Visibility^ dropdown
list.
The state of this variable will determine whether the visualization will be visible:
 If the state of the variable is ON, TRUE or 1, the visualization will be visible.
 If the state of the variable is OFF, FALSE or 0, the visualization will be hidden.
 If the state of the variable is BLINK, the visualization will blink. Use the Blink
Interval property to define how fast the visualization will blink.
 If the variable has another state than the ones mentioned above, the visualization
will be visible.

Blink Interval (ms) Only available if the Blink option is selected in the Visibility dropdown list.
Interval in ms with which the visualization will blink.

Note
  • When the visibility is based on a variable, the visualization will always be visible in the UI and
    when your project is in Edit mode. In Run mode, the visibility as specified by the variable will
    be used.
  • Visualizations that are linked to a detection rather than a process step have some additional
    Visibility properties that define for which Detection State(s) they will be visible. For more
    information, refer to section 5.6.6 Managing visualizations for the detection on 144.

Overrule location, size and angle properties
The location, size and angle properties of some visualizations can set to be dynamic by checking the
Overrule by variables checkbox. This checkbox is available for:

 On a Projector display, and
 Linked to a process step (so not linked to a Detection)
Note
Visualizations that are linked to a dynamic detection will move and rotate with that detection.
In the Location Variables properties, you can define the variables that contain the X, Y and Z
coordinates of the visualization (in mm from the origin). These values define the coordinates of the
lower left point of the visualizations minimum bounding box.
In the Size Variables properties, you can define the variables that contain the length and width of the
visualization, i.e. the size in the X, and Y direction respectively.

Note
When clicking the Set Location Variables to Default button, the values of the variables will
be set to the visualizations coordinates as defined in the Arkite software.
When clicking the Set Size Variables to Default button, the values of the variables will be set
to the visualizations size as defined in the Arkite software.
In the Angle Variable property, you can define a variable that contains an offset to the visualizations
default angle. When the value of this variable changes, the visualization will rotate according to the
variables value.
For example, when the visualization as it is drawn in the software has an angle of 25 degrees in
relation to the X-axis and the Angle Variable has a value of 15, the visualization will be rendered in an
angle of 40 degrees in relation to the X-axis.
By default, the visualization will rotate around its centre, as shown in the image below:
