Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Property Description

Search local folder Only available if the File Name option is selected in the Image Source property.
The folder in which the system will look to find the image to display.
It does not look into subdirectories. The folder is local in that it looks for files in the
specified folder on the workstation on which the project happens to be running. So
different workstations may have a folder with the same name, but it may contain
different files.
Click the icon to select the relevant folder on your workstation.
You can also use different folders on different workstations by storing the local folder
name in a variable. Click the icon and select the variable of your choice.
Alternatively, you can also type the variable name between double braces, i.e.
{{Variable name}}.
Example
Typically, this feature can be used to display a snapshot that was taken in a
Snapshot process step. To make things work, use the same folder you have
specified in the Snapshot folder property in the Snapshot process step. In the
Variable property, use the same variable you have specified in the Name or the
Output last snap shot name to variable property in the Snapshot process step.

The horizontal alignment of the image or video. This can be either left, center or right.

Maintain ratio If checked, the image or video will always have the same width/height ratio, so it will
not be stretched to fill up all available space.

True scale (1:1) Allows to project images on a surface using scale 1:1, which is especially useful to
project CAD drawings.
Both vector (SVG and STL) and image formats (PNG, TIFF) are supported.
Rendering on scale ignores the Maintain ratio and Align properties, as the
coordinates in the source file are respected 1:1.
The accuracy that can be achieved mostly depends on the amount of distortion
introduced by the projector lens. The distortion depends on the type of projector, but
typical values are +/- 0.5%. If the projector is not perpendicular to the surface, the
margin increases with the angle. To achieve best results, accurate calibration of the
projector is a must, and preferably manual projector calibration (from the ribbon) is
used.
Note
For more information on manual projector calibration, refer to 2.3 Other
calibration options on page 28.
As an example, a simple CAD drawing can be found in various formats in:
C:\Program Files\Arkite\Arkite Workstation\Help\CAD

Offset X (mm) Specifies the offset of the image on the X axis.
Only available if True Scale (1:1) is enabled.

Offset Y (mm) Specifies the offset of the image on the Y axis.
Only available if True Scale (1:1) is enabled.

Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Property Description

Show Image in PDF If checked, the image or a thumbnail of the video will be shown in the PDF export.

You can let the software render images based on SVG content. An example use case is where
feedback from a vision system provides areas to highlight, by writing such SVG content to a variable
via the API.
To render images based on SVG content:
 Check the SVG option in the Image Source property
 Check the True Scale (1:1) property.
This allows you to use the world coordinate system (mm) that was established during calibration,
i.e. the coordinates in mm on your table or surface.
Note
If you dont check the True Scale (1:1) property, whatever content you provide will be displayed in
the center of your Image visualization element.

 In the SVG Content property, specify the SVG (Scalable Vector Graphics) content for the image
to be displayed, or the variable containing the SVG content.
You can use standard SVG elements, some typical examples are <circle>, <ellipse>, <line>,
<polyline>, <polygon>, <text> or <rect> (for a rectangle).
For a full overview of SVG elements and their properties, see
https://www.w3schools.com/graphics/svg_intro.asp.
Encoding for SVG elements is UTF-8.
Note 1
While writing your SVG content, take into account the guidelines below:
  • Make sure the coordinates you provide in the SVG contents are within the coordinates of the
    Image visualization element, otherwise you contents will not be visible.
  • Use single quotes rather than double quotes. This simplifies their use in the API.
  • Use the style attribute rather than the individual presentation attributes.
    See https://www.w3.org/TR/SVG/styling.html#StyleAttribute for more information.
  • For colors within the style attribute, you can either use rgb, rgba or hex color codes.
    Named colors are also supported.
  • Be aware that the Y-axis in the Arkite coordinate system is oriented in the opposite direction
    (upwards from the origin) than the one in the SVG coordinate system (downwards from the
    origin). When writing SVG content, the Arkite coordinate system is used, unless you use a full
    SVG document.
Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Note 2
If desired, you can also use a full SVG document, but in that case you need to take into account
that the coordinate system as specified in the SVG document is used as a source and converted
to the Arkite coordinate system (also taking care of the orientation of the Y-axis). By default, SVG
units are in pixels, and if not otherwise scaled, 1 unit = 1 pixel. To ensure that your SVG document
is rendered correctly, include an explicit width and height attribute ensuring the scaling is set to 1
unit = 1 mm.
For example, an SVG document with viewBox= 22 00 0 3350 325  defines a coordinate system
starting at (2200, 0) with a width of 3350 units and a height of 325 units. To ensure the correct
scaling, include width="3350mm" height="325mm".
Below, you can find some examples with the corresponding result:
Example  SVG element, rectangle with blue fill, pink border and 50% opacity
Code
<rect x='50' y='20' width='150' height='150'
style='fill:blue;stroke:pink;stroke-width:5;opacity:0.5' />
Result

Code explanation
  • The width and height attributes of the element define the height and the width of the
    rectangle
  • The style attribute is used to define CSS properties for the rectangle
  • The CSS fill property defines the fill color of the rectangle
  • The CSS stroke property defines the color of the border of the rectangle
  • The CSS stroke-width property defines the width of the border of the rectangle
  • The CSS opacity property defines the opacity value for the whole element (legal range: 0 to
    1)
Example  SVG element, yellow circle
Code
<circle style='fill: yellow' cx='100' cy='50' r='30'/>
Result

Jobs

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Code explanation
  • The cx and cy attributes define the x and y coordinates of the center of the circle. If cx and cy
    are omitted, the circle's center is set to (0,0)
  • The r attribute defines the radius of the circle
Example  SVG element, red polyline
Code
<polyline points='0,40 40,40 40,80 80,80 80,120 120,120 120,160'
style='fill:white;stroke:red;stroke-width:4' />
Result

Code explanation
The points attribute defines the list of points (pairs of x and y coordinates) required to draw the
polyline.

    Tip
    While dragging the visualization with your mouse, visual guidelines will appear that will allow you
    to easily align the visualization. The guidelines below will appear:
    • Guidelines towards the middle of the screen will appear when you reach the middle of the
      screen with an edge or with the middle of the visualization, both horizontally and vertically.
    • Object to object alignment lines appear to help you to align two visualizations with each
      other, both horizontally and vertically. This way, you can align the top, the bottom or the
      middle of the visualizations with each other.
    • Arrows appear to help you to position two visualizations at the same distance from the edge
      or the center of the screen.
    • When you have more than two visualizations, arrows appear when the distance between
      visualizations 1 and 2 is the same as between visualizations 2 and 3. This helps you to ensure
      there is the same distance between visualizations.
    • When you are changing the size of an object, lines appear inside the objects when they have
      the same length or width. This helps you to make the objects have the same size.
  2. In the Properties pane, update the properties of the visualization if needed.
    Note

      overview of visualization types and their properties, refer to sections 4.4.1 Visualization
      types on page 77 and 4.4.2 Visualization properties on page 78.

Several color properties can be set for a visualization or for a DMX light, in case a DMX device is

 Setting a fixed solid color

4.5 Working with conditions

What?
Conditions can be used to specify whether a step should be executed or not. Any individual or
composite process step can be linked to one or more conditions. Only if at least one of the conditions
holds, the step will be executed.
A condition can consist of one or more subconditions.

Project-Wide versus Job-Specific conditions
Conditions can be project-wide or job-specific.
Project-wide conditions can be used in every job in your project, while job-specific conditions can be
used in one job only, and will only be visible if that job is selected.

Jobs

    To add a job-specific condition, first select the relevant job in the ribbon and then select the Job -
    Specific group.

5. Detections

5.1 About detections

A detection is a building block in the Arkite software used to make a representation of your workbench.
By creating detections, you define which tools and components are used during and what activities
take place during your assembly process. Once the detections have been configured in the Arkite
software, you can use them to build your assembly process. This allows the system to guide the
operator and give him the required instructions.
When using Arkites operator guidance platform with Arkite 3D sensor ( Validate and Vision license),
it can also verify certain events or object states. The system will be able to tell your operator whether
all required tools and objects are available and what to do with them. It can validate if an activity has
been executed correctly and if a tool has been returned to its location.
Note
For more information about building your assembly process, refer to chapter 6 Processes on
page 164.

5.2 Project-Wide detections versus Job-Specific detections

Project-Wide detections
Project-wide detections are detections that can be used in all the jobs in your project.
For example the picking bins on your workbench will typically be defined as project-wide detections.

Job-Specific detections
Job-specific detections are detections that can only be used in one specific job. If another job is
selected, you will not be able to see or select such a detection.
For example, activities performed during the assembly of a product will typically be defined as job-
specific detections.

5.3 Detection types

In the table below, you can find a list of available detection types:

Detection type Description

Object Any component or product on the workbench.
When using a Validate or Vision license (= with Arkite 3D sensor), the system will detect
if the object is present or not and can give instructions to place it or take it away.

Detections

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Detection type Description

Tool A tool that is used during the assembly process. When not used, the tool should be at a
fixed location. A tool can also have a shadow board: this is an image of the tool that will
be shown at the default location of the tool when its not present.
In case of a smart tool, the system can ensure that the tool can only be used during the
correct step in the assembly process.
When using a Validate or Vision license (= with Arkite 3D sensor), the system will detect
if a tool is present or not and can give instructions to place it or take it away. For smart
tools, it will not only ensure the tool is enabled at the right moment during the assembly
process, but also at the right location. When the operator wants to use the tool at a wrong
place, the tool will not work.
When using a Vision license (= with Arkite Vision sensor), you can indicate a zone on
your workbench in which a tool may be placed. The software will detect where exactly in
this zone the tool is located and track it when you put it at a different location within the
zone after usage.

Picking bin A storage unit or picking location, containing materials used in the assembly process.
When using a Validate or Vision license (= with Arkite 3D sensor), the system will detect
if the object is present or not and can give instructions to place it or take it away.
Additionally, it can also ask to pick a material from the picking bin and verify if the action
is executed.
Activity An activity that is performed during the assembly process.
When using a Validate or Vision license (= with Arkite 3D sensor), the system can verify
if an activity has been performed by detecting movement at the defined location.
An activity can be linked with a tool.

The expected state of an assembly process at a certain point in time.
The system verifies if a (sub)assembly has been executed correctly by comparing the

assembly and, optionally, with images of results that should be considered wrong.

    External Trigger Variable:
Detections

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

It is possible to use an external system, for example a PLC or another sensor than the one
provided by Arkite, to validate the presence of a detection. If you want to do so, select the
variable containing the information about the detections presence and the define:
External Trigger ON State:
the value that is expected in the External Trigger Variable to activate the detection. To insert
dynamic content, click the icon at the location where you want to include the content and
select the variable containing the dynamic content. Alternatively, you can also type the
variable name between double braces, i.e. {{Variable name}}.
External Trigger ON Time:
the time in milliseconds that the ON state needs to be reached before the detection is
activated.
External Trigger OFF time:
the time in milliseconds the External Trigger variable needs to have another value than the ON
state before the detection is deactivated.

Note
In this case, it is not needed to teach the detection. If you do, the teaching will be ignored by
the system as long as an external trigger has been configured.

 Overrule location by variables:
It is possible to make the location, size and orientation of a detection dynamic, based on the
value of variables. For example, you can teach and finetune the detection in the Arkite
software but let the location be defined by the input of an external system through the Arkite
API.

Note
For more information on working with the Arkite API, refer to chapter 18 The Arkite API on
281.
In the Location Variables properties, you can define the variables that contain the X, Y and Z
coordinates of the detection (in mm from the origin). These values define the coordinates of
the lower left point of the detections minimum bounding box.
In the Size Variables properties, you can define the variables that contain the length, width
and height of the detection, i.e. the size in the X, Y and Z direction respectively.
When changing location and size variables properties, all projections linked to the detection as
well as the picking boxes for a picking bin will move along.
The Projection Z variable allows you to define a different Z value for your projection than the
bottom of your box. If multiple projections are linked to the detection, the Projection Z variable
defines the Z value of the lowest projection. If left blank, the projections Z value maintains its
existing distance to the bottom of the box.
The table below contains some examples of how the Z an projection Z location variables
behave:

 Pick To Light (DMX)
You can link your detection to a DMX light. To do so, you first need to add a Pick To Light

a DMX light that is linked to a detection changes depending on the status of the detection,
based on the Detection colors template. To manage the behavior and the colors that are
used, refer to section 15.2 The Detection Colors template on page 266.

5.6.1 Optimize your sensor stream view

Before you start teaching detections, you should make sure you have the best view possible on your
workbench. To do so, navigate to the Detections tab.

In the Teaching subtab, optimize your sensor stream view:

 In the dropdown, select the view that gives the best result for your specific situation:
 Top down : provides an orthographic projection along the Z-axis, so you have a top-down view
on your calibration surface without a perspective effect. This view is recommended when you
prefer a 2D view, but are working with detections that are high above the calibration surface.
Use your mouse wheel to zoom in or out
Hold your right mouse button and move around to shift your view to the left or the right
 3D: provides a 3D view of your workbench.
Hold your left mouse button and move around to rotate your view

are only meant to increase the visibility of the objects for the user. Changing these settings will not

  1. Optionally, update the settings:
    Setting Description
Detection mode Select the sensor stream or algorithm that is used for teaching the detection:
 Automatic : the system will select the stream with the best contrast. This is the
default option.
 Depth : use the depth stream.
 IR: use the Infrared intensity stream.
 Reflective tape (IR): in some cases, objects are difficult to detect due to a low
contrast or changing light conditions in the working area. This can be solved by
replacing the object with a piece of reflective tape with a high and constant IR value.
For more information, refer to section 5.10 Working with reflective tape (Validate
and Vision license only) on page 157.
 Infrared edges: when selecting this option, the IR stream will be used but the
sensor will look for edges, in other words for the boundaries of an object where there
is a high contrast with the adjacent pixels. It can be used to detect objects regardless
their color or variations in infrared lighting conditions.
 Shape based (Vision license only): use the shape-based matching algorithm.
This algorithm will detect the edges of an object, in order to recognize its shape.
Color and material is mostly ignored. Use this option to create a quality check that
works for the same object in different colors.
 Histogram based (Vision license only): use the histogram-intersection based
matching algorithm.
Use this option for checking:
 Non-rigid shapes, for example a cable that can be bent in various ways or a dot of
glue of which the shape and size may vary.
 Objects with different shades/colors.
Note
Not all colors can be distinguished  the infrared intensity value should differ
sufficiently. For example, yellow and orange are typically hard to tell apart.

Position tolerance Define the accuracy of the size of the box that is created after detection. The options
are:
 Wide : the shape that is 100% larger, i.e. twice the size, than the detected object.
 Narrow: a shape is created that is 50% larger than the detected object. This is the
default option when detecting a tool. This way, the operator does not have to put
back a tool at the exact same location.
 Accurate : a shape is created that is 20% larger than the detected object
 Exact: a shape is created with the same size as the detected object. This is the
default option for other detections.

Detections

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Setting Description

Area of interest Define how the area of interest is defined:
 Automatic: the system will look for differences within the working zone between the
different snapshots.
 Manual: specify the area of interest yourself.
After selecting the Manual option, click the Specify... button. A popup window will
open with an image of the first snapshot. Use the Previous and Next buttons to
browse through snapshots. In the snapshots, you can see the differences as detected
by the system.

 Click Add mask to ignore particular zones.

For tools and objects only.

Note
For objects and tools with an irregular form for which the orientation can vary a lot,
it is recommended to add multiple With Object / With Tool snapshots from
different angles. For each snapshot, indicate the angle by clicking in the lower left
corner of the snapshot and selecting the correct angle.
Watch out:
Rotate the object counterclockwise to indicate an increasing positive angle. For
example, a quarter-turn counterclockwise results in an angle of 90 degrees, a
quarter-turn clockwise results in an angle of -90*.

Adjust projection Define whether projections should be adjusted when teaching the same quality check a
second time. If you have edited the automatically generated projections on the

  1. Click Teach.
Detections

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

For every detection, a box is created with the same size and position as the detected object. This
allows the system to verify whether the object is present.

Important
The system can only detect whether an object is present on the location of the detection. It is not
able to follow an object and check whether it is present on another location on the workbench.
Therefore, it makes sense to integrate a fixture onto the workbench, where the component can be
fixated during the process which makes sure that the entire configuration of components and
detections are standardized and stay in the same location over time.
Only for tools and when using a Vision license, you have the option to define a working zone for
the location of a tool. The system will then follow the position of that tool within the zone.
Additionally, a draw shape visualization is generated on the Projector display, which will be projected
on the workbench when something needs to be done with the detection.

Note
By default, the brush color of this visualization changes depending on the state of the detection,
based on the Detection colors template. To manage the behavior and the colors that are used,
refer to section 15.2 The Detection Colors template on page 266.
For picking bins, a second box is generated right above the picking bin. This allows the system to
detect when something is picked from the picking bin. That works fine, unless you are working with
several (rows of) picking bins stacked upon each other, hiding the boxes from the picking bins below
them to the sensor. For more information on how to deal with stacked picking bins, refer to section
5.11 Working with stacked picking bins on page 158.

Detections

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Setting Description

Detection mode Select the algorithm that is used for teaching the detection:
 Automatic : the system will select the algorithm with the best result. This is the default
option.
 Shape based: use the shape-based matching algorithm.
This algorithm will detect the edges of an object, in order to recognize its shape. Color
and material is mostly ignored. Use this option to create a quality check that works for
the same object in different colors.
 Texture based: use the correlation-based matching algorithm, based on a Normalized
Cross-Correlation (NCC) model.
This algorithm looks for patterns in grey values. As opposed to the shape based
algorithm, it uses all grey values and not only clear edges. Different color and material
will have an impact on the quality check.
 Histogram based: use the histogram-intersection based matching algorithm.
Use this option for checking:
 Non-rigid shapes, for example a cable that can be bent in various ways or a dot of glue
of which the shape and size may vary.
 Objects with different shades/colors.
Note
Not all colors can be distinguished  the infrared intensity value should differ sufficiently.
For example, yellow and orange are typically hard to tell apart.

Position
tolerance

Define the accuracy of the size of the box that is created after detection. The options are:
 Wide : the shape that is 100% larger, i.e. twice the size, than the detected object.
 Narrow: a shape is created that is 50% larger than the detected object.
 Accurate : a shape is created that is 20% larger than the detected object
 Exact: a shape is created with the same size as the detected object. This is the default
option for quality checks.

Area of interest Define how the area of interest is defined:
 Automatic: the system will look for differences within the working zone between the
different snapshots.
 Manual: specify the area of interest yourself.
After selecting the Manual option, click the Specify... button. A popup window will open

snapshots. In the snapshots, you can see the differences as detected by the system.

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Setting Description

Exposure mode Select the camera exposure that will be used for taking the snapshots:
 Automatic : uses the HDR option
 Dark: uses a short exposure, resulting in a darker image
 Normal: uses a medium exposure
 Bright: uses a long exposure, resulting in a brighter image
 HDR: High Dynamic Range. The camera captures multiple frames with different
exposure times, and combines them into one image, selecting the most appropriate
intensity for each part of the image. This allows to perform reliable quality checks on
scenes that contain both bright and darker elements.
Note
In the user interface, by default the HDR image is shown. You can select a different
exposure in the Settings menu.

Adjust projection Define whether projections should be adjusted when teaching the same quality check a
second time. If you have edited the automatically generated projections on the Projector
tab, it is recommended to uncheck this checkbox and adjust the projections yourself after
teaching.

Adjust occlusion
box

Define whether the occlusion box should be adjusted when teaching the same quality
check a second time. If you have edited the automatically generated occlusion box on the
Fine Tune tab, it is recommended to uncheck this checkbox and adjust the projections
yourself after teaching.
  1. Click Teach.
    A box is created with the same size and position as the area where quality check needs to be
    performed. When performing the quality check, the system will compare the live image with all frames
    for all quality check classes. The quality check will be considered successful when the live images
    similarity is the highest for (one of the) frame(s) for a class with type CORRECT and more than the
    minimum percentage as defined in the Detection Rate property on the Finetune tab.
    Examples
    • In the example below, the quality check will be successful because there is a 9 9 % similarity
      with one of the Expected Result frames (type CORRECT), and there is no higher similarity
      with one of the other frames.

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  • In the example below, the quality check will be unsuccessful because there is a 81 % similarity
    with one of the frames in class Not fully inserted with type WRONG, and there is no higher
    similarity with one of the other frames.
Additional to the detection box, an occluder box will also be generated using the Arkite 3D sensor. If
the occlusion rate exceeds the minimum rate, the system will wait to evaluate the quality check until
the occlusion is gone. This prevents a quality check from being classified as wrong while an operator
is still working on it. In case the result is not satisfactory, the occluder box can be edited on the
Finetune tab.

5.6.3 Test a detection

After a detection has been taught, always test whether the teaching has been successful:

 Place the object or tool and take it away and check if the state of the detection gets updated.
 Pick material from a picking bin and check if the system detects it.

 Press a virtual button and check whether the system detects this.
If you are not satisfied with the result, you can either reteach the detection or finetune the detection.

5.6.4 Reteach a detection.................................................................................

If you are not satisfied with a detection, you can decide to reteach it:
  1. Under Detections , select the detection you want to finetune.
  2. In the Teaching subtab, define the settings you want to use for reteaching, e.g.
    Make new Without and With snapshots
    Note
    You can also remove snapshots by clicking the cross in the right-upper corner of the snapshot.
Change the teaching properties, such as the Detection mode or the Position tolerance.
  1. Check the Adjust projection checkbox if you want to visualizations on the Projector tab to be
    updated along with the new detection.
    If you havent changed anything to the visualization generated by the system, you can safely
    use this option
    If you have edited the visualization generated by the system or added extra visualizations, it is
    recommended to uncheck this checkbox, since the system will otherwise undo your changes.
  2. Check the Adjust occlusion box checkbox if you want to occlusion box to be updated along with
    the new detection.
    If you havent changed anything to the occlusion box generated by the system, you can safely
    use this option
 If you have edited the automatically generated occlusion box on the Fine Tune tab, it is
recommended to uncheck this checkbox, since the system will otherwise undo your changes.

Detections

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. Click Teach to apply your changes and reteach the detection.
    Click Cancel to revert your changes.
    Note
    You can also remove all teaching data by right-clicking the detection and selecting Clear
    Teaching.

5.6.5 Finetune a detection

After a detection has been taught, you can tweak the boxes that have been generated in the Finetune
subtab.
  1. Under Detections , select the detection you want to finetune.
  2. In the Finetune subtab, select the box you want to finetune.
  3. Click the Edit button above the image.
  4. Change the size and position of the box by dragging the angular points with your mouse. The
    same can be achieved by updating the coordinates in the Properties panel.
Detections

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Right-click an angular point and select Remove Point to delete it or Insert Point to add an
additional angular point.
  1. Update the properties of the box in the Properties panel:
    Property Description
Z-Coordinates Change the position of the box in relation to the workbench by updating the Base^
z-coordinate or the Height of the box.

Calculation properties for detections taught with detection mode Depth or IR

Use IR Check the checkbox to use the Infrared stream.
Uncheck the checkbox to use the Depth stream.
Image processing Select an image processing filter if needed:
 Background subtraction (depth stream) : filters away all background, so only
the moving foreground objects are visible.
The Reset Background button sets the current situation to be the background.
 Edge detection (IR stream) : the sensor will look for edges, in other words for
the boundaries of an object where there is a high contrast with the adjacent
pixels. It can be used to detect objects regardless their color or variations in
infrared lighting conditions.
IR intensity Define the minimum and maximum IR intensity in the box that is required to
consider an object as present.

Detection rate Define the minimum and maximum percentage of fill rate (or edge rate when Edge
detection is used) of the box that is required to consider an object as present.

Calculation properties for detections taught with detection mode Shape Based, Texture Based or Histogram Based
(Vision license only)

Calculation Type Algorithm that is used for calculating the detection:
 Shape based: use the shape-based matching algorithm.
This algorithm will detect the edges of an object, in order to recognize its shape.
Color and material is mostly ignored. Use this option to create a quality check
that works for the same object in different colors.
 Texture based: use the correlation-based matching algorithm, based on a
Normalized Cross-Correlation (NCC) model.
This algorithm looks for patterns in grey values. As opposed to the shape based
algorithm, it uses all grey values and not only clear edges. Different color and
material will have an impact on the quality check.
 Histogram based: use the histogram-intersection based matching algorithm.
Use this option for checking:
 Non-rigid shapes, for example a cable that can be bent in various ways or a
dot of glue of which the shape and size may vary.
 Objects with different shades/colors.
Note
Not all colors can be distinguished  the infrared intensity value should differ
sufficiently. For example, yellow and orange are typically hard to tell apart.

Detection rate Define the minimum and maximum percentage of fill rate^ of the box that is required
to consider an object as present.
For Quality checks, this is the minimum percentage of similarity that is needed to
classify the detection as correct.

Position X (mm) Define the difference in position in the X direction that is acceptable.
Only available when Verify Position has been selected when teaching the
detection.

Property Description

Position Y (mm) Define the difference in position in the Y direction that is acceptable.
Only available when Verify Position has been selected when teaching the
detection.

Orientation () Define the difference in orientation that is acceptable.
Only available when Verify Orientation has been selected when teaching the
detection.

Symmetric Orientations Define how many symmetric orientations should be accepted when validating the
detection. The value for this property can be between 1 and 360, with default value
1.
Example
If you are validating an object that is symmetrical along the X axis, the software
will sometimes perceive its orientation as 0 and sometimes as 180 since both
orientations look identical. In this case, set 2 as a value to accept both
orientations.
In case you are checking a 36-teeth gear, set 36 as a value to accept all
possible orientation values. Be aware you should also decrease the default
value of 5 for the Orientation Tolerance property in this case, otherwise you
will end up accepting any orientation.
Only available when Verify Orientation has been selected when teaching the
detection.

Occlusion Check the Occlusion logic checkbox if you want the system to verify if the object
is hidden.
The Min Rate dropdown list contains the minimal percentage of occlusion that is
required to consider the object as hidden.
Time thresholds (ms) Define for how long an object needs to be within (ON) or outside (OFF) the range
defined in the fill rate properties to change the detection state.
For activities, you can disable the OFF setting. To do so, uncheck the Wait for
OFF checkbox. In this case, an activity does not need to be deactivated to proceed
to the next step when used in a process.
In case the Experience Level functionality is enabled, a percentage of these time
thresholds is used for every specific experience level.
Note
For more information on the Experience Level functionality, refer to chapter 8
Experience levels on page 224.
To overrule the default percentages for this specific detection, check the Overrule
exp defaults checkbox. After checking this checkbox, the system will fall back to
100% for level 1, 50% for level 2 and 20% for level 3. You can update these
percentages as required.

To change the default percentages for all detections, refer to section 8.3
Experience level settings on page 225.

Detections

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Property Description

Coordinates Change the position of the box by updating the X and Y coordinates of the angular
points.
Note
You can also change the size and position of the box by dragging the angular
points with your mouse.

Tip
While dragging the visualization with your mouse, visual guidelines will appear that will allow you
to easily align the visualization. The guidelines below will appear:
  • Guidelines towards the middle of the screen will appear when you reach the middle of the
    screen with an edge or with the middle of the visualization, both horizontally and vertically.
  • Object to object alignment lines appear to help you to align two visualizations with each
    other, both horizontally and vertically. This way, you can align the top, the bottom or the
    middle of the visualizations with each other.
  • Arrows appear to help you to position two visualizations at the same distance from the edge
    or the center of the screen.
  • When you have more than two visualizations, arrows appear when the distance between
    visualizations 1 and 2 is the same as between visualizations 2 and 3. This helps you to ensure
    there is the same distance between visualizations.
  • When you are changing the size of an object, lines appear inside the objects when they have
    the same length or width. This helps you to make the objects have the same size.

 On : the visualization will always be visible
 Blink : the visualization will blink. Use the Blink Interval property to define how
fast the visualization will blink.
 Based on Variable : the visibility of the visualization will be based on the current
state of the variable provided in the Variable for visibility property.

Variable for visibility Only available if the Based on Variable option is selected in the Visibility^ dropdown
list.
The state of this variable will determine whether the visualization will be visible:
 If the state of the variable is ON, TRUE or 1, the visualization will be visible.
 If the state of the variable is OFF, FALSE or 0, the visualization will be hidden.

checkboxes

For example:
 For an object, the Place and Take checkboxes are checked by default.

and Take visualizations that match the empty space on the workstation and the top
surface of the object respectively.
 For a picking bin, the Place , Take, Pick, Detection Error and Picking Error
checkboxes are checked by default.
However, it can be valuable to make a visualization for Place , Take and Detection
Error , matching the entire picking bin size, and a different smaller visualization for
Pick and Picking error , matching the picking bin picking entrance.

    The materials from the CSV file will be imported into your project.

5.9 Working with smart tools....................................................................................

What
Smart tools are tools that can communicate with external systems, such as the Arkite software.
Through the Arkite software, they can be configured in such a way that they can only be used during
the correct step in the assembly process. When using a Validate or Vision license (= with Arkite 3D
sensor), the system will also ensure the smart tool can only be used at the correct location.

Detections

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

How to configure smart tools using Open Protocol communication
To configure a smart tool using Open Protocol communication, execute the following steps:
  1. Make sure your smart tool is on the same network as your workstation.
  2. In the Connectivity tab under Communication , click the Add button and select Open Protocol.
A new card for the Open Protocol communication module is added to the list of communication
modules.
  1. In the Properties pane, configure the properties for the communication module.
    Property Description
Name Name of the communication module
Note
Next to the Name label, the object ID for the communication module is shown.
You can copy it to use it when working with the Arkite API.

Log Table The table name in the logging database in which all incoming and outgoing
messages and exceptions will be logged.
Automatic Smart Tool
Settings

If this checkbox is enabled, the required variables for communication with a smart
tool will be generated and configured.
IP Address The IP address of the remove device, for example: 10.0.11.12.

Device Type  When using Atlas Copcos MicroTorque Controller MTF6000, select MTFocus
6000.
 For all other devices, select Generic.

Port The TCP/IP port to use. Default for open protocol communication is 4545.
Start communication
revision

When an open protocol communication actuator is first sparked, a start
communication message will be sent to the controller. This message contains a 3
digit revision. For most controllers, this revision is 001. Check the manual of your
controller to check for divergent revisions.
End communication revision When the module is paused, an end communication message will be sent to the
controller. This message contains a 3 digit revision. For most controllers, this
revision is 001. Check the manual of your controller to check for divergent
revisions.
Stop String Type Every message will be ended by a special ending character. The default value is
null (null character). Other types include a CRLF (carriage return line feed) and #.

Log Keep Alive messages Every incoming, outgoing and exception message will be logged. However, to keep
the connection with the controller open, keep alive messages will be sent (and
received) every ten seconds. In most situations, you dont want to see these
messages cluttering your message stream. However, if you would like to see these
messages, please check this checkbox.

5.10 Working with reflective tape (Validate and Vision license only)

What
In some cases, objects are difficult to detect due to a low contrast or changing light conditions in the
working area. This can be solved by replacing the object with a piece of reflective tape with a high and
constant IR value.

How to use reflective tape option 1

  1. Replace the object on your working bench with a piece of reflective tape of the same size.
  2. Teach the system the location of this reflective tape, using the Sensor Mode Reflective tape.
    For more information, refer to section 5.6.2 Teaching detections on page 127.
  3. On the Finetune tab, change the Fill Rate fields:
    When working with reflective tape, the object is present when the reflective tape cannot be
    detected. For example, if a 70-100% range is used to detect if the reflective tape is present, you
    should change the range to 0-70% in order to let the system detect correctly the reflective tape is
    covered by the present object.
    For more information, refer to section 5.6.5 Finetune a detection on page 141.
Detections

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

How to use reflective tape option 2

  1. Replace the object on your working bench with a piece of reflective tape of the same size.
  2. Teach the system the location of this reflective tape, using the Sensor Mode Reflective tape.
    Use the snapshot with the tape in the Without image.
    Use the snapshot without the tape in the With image.
    For more information, refer to section 5.6.2 Teaching detections on page 127.

5.11 Working with stacked picking bins (Validate and Vision license only)

What?
In many cases, several picking bins will be stacked upon each other on the workbench. Except for the
top row, the picking bins will therefore be hidden from the sensors view and the system wont be able
to see them. In this chapter, a workaround for this issue is explained.

How to work with stacked picking bins
When a picking bin is taught, the system automatically creates two boxes:

 A box to detect if the picking bin is present
 A box to detect right above this box to detect the operators hand when picking material from the
picking bin.
When working with stacked picking bins, the boxes for all picking bins will by default be all on top of
each other, and the system will only be able to detect the upper row of picking bins. This is not really a
problem for detecting picking bin presence, since they will only be removed very rarely.
However, to successfully detect picking materials, you should move the corresponding boxes in front
of the actual picking bins and make them a lot smaller. You should set them in such a way that they
form a small cuboid gate at the entrance of the picking bin. As a result, the boxes wont be occluded
to the sensor and the system can successfully detect the operators hand going into the correct picking
bin and picking a material. For more information on how to edit the pick material boxes, refer to
section 5.6.5 Finetune a detection on page 141.

Detections

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

5.12 Working with mobile picking racks (Validate and Vision license only)

What?
In complex assembly processes, many materials are required to complete an assembly. In such a
case, picking bins are often organized in different mobile picking racks that are exchanged during the
assembly so that the relevant materials are available at all times.
It is important the Arkite Operator Guidance system only calculates the presence of the picking bins in
the active picking rack, to avoid error visualizations for picking bins that are not there.

How to work with mobile picking racks

  1. Put a mobile picking rack on its in-use location and teach all the picking bins in the picking rack.
  2. Repeat this for all mobile picking racks.
  3. Add a detection group for each picking rack, and move all picking bins into the applicable group.
  4. Create a variable for each picking rack.
  5. Set the Enabled property for the detection group to Based on variable.
  6. In the Based on variable property, select the variable you created for the picking rack the picking
    bin belongs to.
  7. In your assembly process, each time you exchange picking racks, set the value of the variable for
    the active picking rack to ON and the value of the variable for all other picking racks to OFF.
Detections

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

5.13 CAD/CAM detections (Validate and Vision license only)

5.13.1 About CAD/CAM detections.....................................................................

CAD/CAM detections allow to create a detection where the size and location in 3D space is based on
a CAD model.
CAD/CAM detections are just like other detections (objects, tools ...), but their location in 3D space is
provided by both a 3D model (.STL file) and a transformation matrix that positions the CAD model in
space. Such a transformation is typically provided by the CAD/CAM system. All other properties (such
as which sensor to use) are taken from the template.

5.13.2 Adding CAD/CAM detections

To add a CAD/CAM detection, execute the steps below:
  1. Navigate to the Detections tab.
  2. Click the New button and select Object.
  3. Teach the object as described in section Teach an object, picking bin, tool or virtual button on
    page 127.
  4. Click the New button and select CAD/CAM Detection.
    The New CAD/CAM Detection window appears.
  5. Provide the input below:
    Field Description
Template detection Select the object you have taught in step 3.
All properties of the CAD/CAM detection will be identical to the one selected as template,
except its location in 3D space. Such properties include which sensor to use, fill rate
thresholds, whether it is depth or IR etc.

3D object The 3D object, which is provided as an STL file (Standard Triangle Language). STL is a
simple and commonly used file format, to which any CAD program can export.
To select an STL file, click the 3 dots. In the Please select an image window, select From
File in the New menu.

Detections

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Field Description

Transformation matrix Specifies how the 3D object is positioned in 3D space, relative to the coordinate system
that was defined during calibration. Such a matrix is usually provided by the CAD/CAM
system, and allows to translate, rotate and scale the object as needed.
The first three columns specify the XYZ-coordinates of where the X-axis, Y-axis and Z-axis
of the 3D object should end up respectively.
The last column specifies the translation, i.e. where the origin of the 3D object is moved to.
The default values specify an identity matrix, which means the 3D object is used as-is,
without transforming it.
Generate projections The locations of the projections are calculated based on the provided 3D object and the
accompanying transformation matrix. If multiple projectors are used, the most suitable
projector is by default chosen for the projections ( Calculate best projector option). Say
you have two projectors that cover the left and right areas. A detection on the left area will
use the left projector, and a detection on the right will automatically pick the right projector.
If the Preserve projector(s) from template option is selected, the locations of the
projections are still calculated, but they will use the same projector as the template. This
option is more suitable if you want fine-grained control on which projector will be used, or if
you want to use all projectors in which case the template should also define projections for
all projectors.
  1. Click Teach.
Result
Your detection is updated with the information from the STL file.

5.13.3 Example 1: no transformation

Template detection
Create a detection of type Object , and use all default settings.

6. Processes

6.1 About processes

What?
Next to your job assembly, you can configure different processes in the Arkite software. Processes run
in parallel with job execution.
When you create a project, by default one process called Operator Job Selection will be available
that is started when the project is loaded. This process takes care of job selection and execution.
Additionally, you may need more processes to, for example::
 Log data
 Send data to a communication module
 Initialize parameters when a project is started

 Configure the behavior of a touch screen
 ...

6.2 Generating Job Selection processes..................................................................

What?
With the Generate menu, you can add a job selection process yourself.

You can use the Generate menu to:

 Add the Operator Job Selection process to an existing project, made in a software version
before 2025.1
 Bring back the Operator Job Selection process if you have accidentally removed it
 Replace the default Operator Job Selection process with another job selection option:
 Operator job selection without quantity

 MES/ERP job selection example
Note
  • Only one of these processes should be active at a time. Therefore, if you add another option,
    the Project Loader trigger of the existing process will be removed.
  • For a better understanding of the different steps in the job selection processes, read the
    comments that are added in the software.
Processes

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Operator job selection
The Operator job selection process is the one that is present by default in a new project.
It consists of three major steps in which an operator:

 Selects a job from a gallery on the touch screen
 Selects a variant from a gallery on the touch screen
 Enters a quantity on the touch screen

After the selection, the selected job variant is executed the specified number of times. After the last
iteration, the job selection is automatically started again.
When you add new jobs or new job variants, these are automatically added to the galleries on the
selection screens.
Warning
If you havent configured any job variants, the job will be executed skipping all optional steps (if
there are any).

Operator job selection without quantity
The Operator job selection without quantity process consists of two major steps in which an
operator:
 Selects a job from a gallery on the touch screen
 Selects a variant from a gallery on the touch screen

After the selection, the selected job variant is executed in a loop until the operator stops the execution
using the Close button on the Job screen. After that, the job selection is automatically started again.
When you add new jobs or new job variants, these are automatically added to the galleries on the
selection screens.
Warning
If you havent configured any job variants, the job will be executed skipping all optional steps (if
there are any).

MES/ERP job selection example
The MES/ERP job selection example process consists of a steps in which a job order containing job,
variant and quantity is retrieved from a MES/ERP system.
When adding this process, an HTTP communication module and an example job is added at the same
time.

Processes

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

In the first step of the process, Arkite connects to the Arkite MES and retrieves a JSON file. You will
need to update the URL in the Properties of that step to have it connect to your own MES.
In the subsequent steps, the job, variant and quantity is retrieved from the work order and written into
variables in Arkite. Depending on the input from your MES, you may have to update these steps as
well.

6.3 Adding a new process

To add a new process, execute the steps below:
  1. On the Processes tab, click New Process.
The process is added to the list of processes.
  1. In the Properties pane, update the name of your process to something meaningful.
  2. By default, one text instructions and image instructions variable is generated for all instructions for
    all processes. If you want to define a specific variable for the process you add, you can change
    the variable here.
Note
When you define specific variables, you will also have to add a specific text and image
visualizations to your process that displays the state of those variables.
  1. By default, a process is started when the project is loaded. Optionally, update the trigger(s) by
    which the process is started:
 Under Start by trigger , click the + button to add a trigger.

 Select the appropriate trigger.

 Configure the trigger properties.

Processes

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Note
In the next section, you can find an overview of all process triggers and their properties.

Result
Your process is set up now. You can start configuring process steps to build the contents of your
process.

6.4.1 Alarm Clock

About the Alarm Clock trigger
The Alarm Clock trigger allows you to start a process every day at a specified point in time. This point
in time can be defined as a static value or as a variable.

Note
If there is no variable selected or if the format is incorrect, the time will be 00:00:00 by default.

Use variables for time Check this checkbox to use the value of a variable rather than a fixed time.
Time The time at which the process should start.

Variable for time The variable in the time at which the process should start is stored.

6.4.3 Receive Communication

About the Receive Communication trigger
The Receive Communication trigger allows you to start a process within your project when data is
received from an external device, such as a PLC, a smart tool, a database, a barcode scanner or
another workstation.
The communication is done through a communication module. Before you can use a receive
communication trigger, you first need to add and configure the appropriate communication module.
Click the + icon in the Communication drop-down list.

Note
For more information regarding the next steps, refer to the section 7.3.3 Adding a
communication module on page 205.

Common properties
For every Receive Communication trigger, the properties below need to be configured:

Property Description

Name Name for your Receive Communication^ trigger. By default, the name of the
communication module you have selected is used, but you can change it.
Note
Next to the Name label, the object ID for the trigger is shown. You can copy it to
use it when working with the Arkite API. For more information about the Arkite
API, refer to chapter 18 The Arkite API on page 281.

Communication Module Communication module that is used to receive the communication.
The other properties depend on the communication module you have selected for communication.
They are listed below for every available communication module.

Inter-Workstation
Property Description

Variables When the variable(s) you indicate here are received^ from the other workstation, the
process will be started.
Check the All Variables checkbox to start the process when receiving any
variable.

Modbus TCP
Property Description

Variable The variable that will be used to store the received messages.

Processes

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Property Description

Address Type The object type of the read action. It is possible to read:
 Discrete inputs: read-only entity with a size of 1 bit (ON/OFF)
 Coils : read-write entity with a size of 1 bit (ON/OFF)
 Input registers: read-only entity with a size of 16 bits (0-65 535)
 Holding registers: read-write entity with a size of 16 bits (0-65 535)

Address The address of the object from which will be read.
The process will be started when a message is received from the address specified
here, with the correct type.

Open Protocol
Property Description

MID to filter on The MID (which is character 5 to 8 of the message header) to filter the messages
on.
If this field is filled in, only messages with a matching MID will be captured and the
process will only be started when the matching MID is received.
If this field is left empty, all messages will be captured. The process will started
whenever a message is received.

Variable for message The variable that will be used to store the received messages.

6.4.5 Watchdog

About the Watchdog trigger
The Watchdog trigger allows you to let a process run as long as no errors in hardware of software are
detected. The watchdog will check the system with a certain interval and flag possible malfunctions.

Note
Combined with an ethernet communication module and external hardware like a light or buzzer, it
can be used to visualize the state of your system.

Processes

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Properties
Property Description

Name The name for the trigger.
Note
Next to the Name label, the object ID for the trigger is shown. You can copy it to
use it when working with the Arkite API. For more information about the Arkite
API, refer to chapter 18 The Arkite API on page 281.

Milliseconds between ticks The interval with which the watchdog checks the systems hardware and software
features.
Minimum FPS The minimum frames per second the sensor should have.

Variable for message The variable that will store the state of the watchdog (OK or FAILURE). The
process will only start when the state of this variable is OK.

Variable for failure The variable that will store the watchdogs error message when its state is
FAILURE

6.4.6 Variable Changed

About the Variable Changed trigger
The Variable Changed trigger allows you to start a process as soon as one or more variables reach a
certain state or are changed.

Properties

Property Description

Name The name for the trigger.
Note
Next to the Name label, the object ID for the trigger is shown. You can
copy it to use it when working with the Arkite API. For more information
about the Arkite API, refer to chapter 18 The Arkite API on page 281.

Any change Check this checkbox to start the process at any change in state. In this case,
there is no desired state.

Compare with Check this checkbox to use the state of another variable as the desired state.
Variables Define the variable(s) you want to monitor for state change.

Comparison Select a compare operator
Other variable Define the variable you want to compare the variable you monitor with.

Desired state Define which state the variable(s) should reach to start the process
Type  Select AND if all variables need to reach the desired state.
 Select OR if only one of the variables need to reach the desired state.
 Select Probing to use the probing algorithm. More information about can
be found below this table.

State to set (probing) The probing algorithm will select 1 variable. The state of this variable will be
set to the value in this property for 1 ms. After that, it returns to its previous
state. You can use this change to make a change to another variable.

Processes

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Property Description

Premature Probing Spark If not checked, the probing algorithm will wait until all variables have returned
to their default values. Then it will select the variable that has been in the
desired state for the longest time.
If checked, the probing algorithm will select a variable when it has reached
desired state for a significantly longer time than any other variable.

Premature Spark Time Set the minimum time in milliseconds before the probing algorithm selects a
variable.

Premature Spark Fraction Define how much longer a variable needs to be in the desired state than any
other variable for the probing algorithm to select it.

Probing
In case you select probing, there are two possibilities for the start of your process:
 When Premature Probing Spark is not checked, your process will be started when all variables
have reached the desired state at one point and returned to their default state afterwards.
 When Premature Probing Spark is checked, your process will be started:

 When the time set in the Premature Spark Time property has passed, AND
 When one variable was in the desired state significantly longer than any of the other variables.
To define what is significantly longer, the time set in the Premature Spark Fraction is taken
into account.
In both cases, the variable that was in the desired state for the longest time is changed to the value
defined in the property State to Set (probing) for 1 ms. After that, it returns to its previous state.

Example
Suppose we have:
 2 variables with default state OFF.
 Probing is selected, with desired state ON and state to set PROBING
 Variable 1 changes to state ON after 1 second

 Variable 2 changes to state ON after 4 seconds
 Both variables go back to their default state OFF after 5 seconds.

Processes

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

In case Premature Probing Spark is not checked, the behaviour will be as in the table below.
The process is started after 5 seconds, when both variables are back in their default state.
The probing algorithm selects variable 1 because it has been in state ON for the longest time and
changes its state to PROBING for 1 ms.

Time (ms) Variable 1 Variable 2 Process status

0 OFF OFF Not started

1000 ON OFF Not started
2000 ON OFF Not started
3000 ON OFF Not started

4000 ON ON Not started
5000 OFF OFF Started
5001 PROBING OFF Running

5002 OFF OFF Running
6000 OFF OFF Running

In case Premature Probing Spark is checked with both Premature Spark Time and Premature
Spark Fraction set at 2000 ms, the behaviour will be as in the table below.
The process is started after 3 seconds, when variable 1 has been in state ON for 2 seconds longer
than variable 2.

Processes

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

The probing algorithm selects variable 1 and changes its state to PROBING for 1 ms.

Time (ms) Variable 1 Variable 2 Process status

0 OFF OFF Not started
1000 ON OFF Not started

2000 ON OFF Not started
3000 ON OFF Started

3001 PROBING OFF Running
3002 ON OFF Running

4000 ON ON Running
5000 OFF OFF Running
6000 OFF OFF Running

6.5 Configuring process steps

6.5.1 Process step types

A vast amount of process steps types are available to you to build your process. They are divided in
the categories below:
 General steps : some basic, often used process steps.
 Variables : process steps that use the values of a variable as an input or an output.
 Detections : process steps related to the detections you have added

 Materials: process steps related to the materials you have configured.
 Screen buttons: process steps related to the buttons you have added to the touch screen.
 Communication: process steps related to the communication modules you have configured.
 Extra : a number of advanced, less often used process steps.
The available step types are mostly the same as the ones that are available for your job steps on the
Steps tab.
For more information, refer to section 4.3.3 Step types on page 65.
The sections below contain an overview of process types that are available additionally on the
Processes tab.

Processes

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

General steps
Process step type Description

Execute Job Launches a job, specifying a job variant or values for the different job options.
The step will remain active until the job is completed, and is used to calculate the
jobs cycle time. When the process containing the Execute Job step is paused,
the Cycle Time will also be paused.
The cycle time is stored in the variables Cycle Time (format HH:mm:ss) and
Cycle Time Sec (format ss). This allow you to easily display the Cycle Time on a
Projector or a Screen using a Text visualization.
The cycle time is also used in the Cycle Time dashboard. For more information
about dashboarding, refer to chapter 12 Dashboarding on page 248.

Extra

Process step type Description

Open/Close Display Open or close a particular display.

Project Loader Restart the current project or load another project.
Switch Language Sets the language in which instructions are displayed.
Note
By default, instructions are displayed in the user language of the user that is logged
in. If no instructions are available in that language, the system will look for a similar
language. For example, if the user language is en-GB, en-US will be used. If no
similar language is available, the first instruction language in the project will be
used.

Switch User Logs out the current user.
You can indicate a new user to sign in with, or show a login screen.
System Command Issues one of the system commands below:
 Shut down: shut down your workstation
 Reboot: reboot your workstation
 Restart Arkite: close and restart the Arkite software
 Project: open the Projects overview

6.6 Managing visualizations for your process steps

What?
After creating your process steps, you can manage the visualizations that will be displayed when
those steps are active, on a connected projector or screen.
You will see a subtab for every display that is available. By default, a Projector subtab will always be
available.

Note
  • When you have created the project before calibrating, a Projector display is added with the
    screen resolution of the device you are working on (e.g. your laptop). This may not match with
    the actual projector resolution, used during calibration. This will cause projections to be faulty.
    A message on the Projector subtab will warn you for this. Click Fix and update the
    Resolution property to the correct value in the projectors Properties pane.
  • To add more displays, refer to section 7.2.3 Adding a display on page 186.
    When creating a process, the Arkite software will automatically generate visualizations to display text
    and image instructions.
    Additionally, you may also create more visualizations to display.
    When the Experience Level functionality is enabled, you can add experience level buttons to a
    Screen display to allow an operator to select his experience level.

your job steps, as configured on the Steps tab.
For more information, refer to section 4.4 Managing visualizations for your job steps on page 76.

6.7 Working with conditions

What?
Conditions can be used to specify whether a process step should be executed or not. Any individual or
composite process step can be linked to one or more conditions. Only if at least one of the conditions
holds, the step will be executed.
A condition can consist of one or more subconditions.
You can use conditions in your processes in the same way you use them in your jobs on the Steps
tab. For more information, refer to section 4.5 Working with conditions on page 110.

6.8 Working with tasks

What?
Tasks allow you to easily re-use a step or a group of steps across multiple jobs.
Whenever you make changes to a task, those changes will automatically be applied at every location
where you have used the task.

Adding tasks
To add a task, execute the steps below:
  1. In the ribbon, click the Tasks button.
The Tasks tab is added to the list of tabs.

On the ribbon you can switch between Run and Edit mode.

When you make any changes to your project, it automatically switches to Edit mode.
When a project is (re)loaded or a process is started, it automatically switches to Run mode.
In EDIT mode:

 Processes are not running
 Projection of currently selected component or step is visible
This makes it possible to finetune projections on the spot.
In RUN mode:

 Processes are running
 Projection of currently active step is visible
Note
On an editor, i.e. a workstation without a valid Guide , Validate or Vision license, you will be able
to run a project for a maximum of 15 minutes. After that, it will automatically revert to Edit mode.

7. Connectivity

7.1 About connectivity

The Arkite software allows to connect a variety of peripheral devices:
 Displays, i.e. projectors and (touch)screens that are connected.
 Sensors, i.e. the Arkite 3D sensor, the Arkite Vision sensor (when using a Vision license) and, if
applicable, an RGB camera or webcam that is connected
 Communication modules, enabling the system to communicate to external devices.

7.2 Displays

7.2.1 What?

Once your project has been configured, the Arkite software will be able to provide your operators with
real-time picking and assembly instructions through Augmented Reality. These instructions are
provided on one or more displays.

7.2.2 Display types

Two types of displays can be distinguished:
 Projector :
One or more projectors are mounted above the workbench. These projectors enable you to show
instructions on the workbench at the time the operator needs them.

Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

 Screen :
A (touch)screen can be connected to the workstation. On the screen, information and instructions
can be displayed, as well as buttons to interact with the operator.

7.2.3 Adding a display

Steps
To add a display, execute the steps below:
  1. Navigate to the Connectivity tab.
  2. Under Displays , click the Add button and select the display type you want to add.
A new display card is added.
  1. In the Properties pane, configure the properties for the display.
Projector Properties
Note
It is also possible to communicate with a PJLink supported projector by adding a Projector
process step to your process. The PJLink protocol uses an ethernet connection. It can for example
turn the projector on or off, or switch the input source.
For instructions on installing and configuring an Optoma ZH420 projector (our standard projector),
please consult our Arkite hardware installation guide on our customer portal.
For instructions on installing and configuring an Optoma ZW400 projector, you can download the
procedure How to configure the Optoma ZW400 projector for use with Arkite from our
customer portal.
For instructions on configuring a Casio projector, you can download the procedure How to
configure Casio XJ-F210WN For PJ link Control from our customer portal.

Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Next to the Name label, the object ID for the projector is shown. You can copy it
to use it when working with the Arkite API. For more information about the
Arkite API, refer to chapter 18 The Arkite API on page 281.

Auto Show When checked, this display will be shown when the project is opened.
Background Color The displays background color.

Resolution Select the resolution for the display.
Note
When you have created the project before calibrating, a Projector display is
added with the screen resolution of the device you are working on (e.g. your
laptop). This may not match with the actual projector resolution, used during
calibration. This will cause projections to be faulty. Update the Resolution
property to the correct value to fix this.

Display Device Select the display device on which the projector will be shown.

Log Table The table name in the logging database in which all incoming and outgoing
messages and exceptions will be logged.
Note
The logging database is configured in the server settings. For more information,
refer to section 13.3 Changing the logging database, the logging database
and the cleanup of old data on page 254.

Projector IP address The IP Address of the connected PJLink supported projector.

Port The Port of the connected PJLink supported projector. PJLink has a default port of
4352.

7.2.4 Managing displays

 To duplicate a display, select it, click the ... button in the lower-right corner of the card and select
Duplicate.
 To delete a display, select it, click the ... button in the lower-right corner of the card and select
Delete.

 Select a display and click the Show icon to immediately display it.
Tip
If youre not working at the workbench location, you can choose to show the display on the screen
of your pc.
Note
You can show all displays at any time by clicking the Show All Displays button in the ribbon.

 Select a display and click Test to verify which display is connected. The display will be bright
yellow for 5 seconds to help you differentiate it from other displays.

 To turn a Projector display on or off, select it, click the power icon and select Turn on or Turn
off.

7.3 Communication modules

7.3.1 What?

The Arkite software allows to configure a variety of communication modules, enabling the system to
communicate to external devices.

Note
A lot of communication modules use the workstations ethernet ports. Always make sure the
workstations IP address and the IP address of the device youre trying to communicate with, are
within the same range. Remember that the workstation has 2 separate network cards, each with
its own settings.

Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

7.3.2 Communication module types

Barcode / QR Code Scanner
The Barcode / QR Code Scanner communication module is used to connect barcode and QR code
scanners to the workstation through USB. Such scanners are widely used for product recognition.
They convert a barcode or QR code to a specified combination of letters and numbers, or in other
characters. This communication module can also be used as a keyboard logger or to connect an NFC
reader, a foot pedal or hardware button. In the table below, you can find the properties you can
configure for this communication module type.
Note
  • A barcode scanner technically works in the same way as a keyboard. If the scanned barcode
    appears incorrectly, please verify whether the Windows keyboard layout matches with the
    scanner.
  • The Arkite software expects each barcode to end with a carriage return/line feed suffix. Make
    sure to correctly configure this in your barcode scanners settings.
Property Description

Name Name of the communication module
Note
Next to the Name label, the object ID for the communication module is shown.
You can copy it to use it when working with the Arkite API. For more information
about the Arkite API, refer to chapter 18 The Arkite API on page 281.

Log Table The table name in the logging database in which^ all incoming and outgoing
messages and exceptions will be logged.
Note
The logging database is configured in the server settings. For more information,
refer to section 13.3 Changing the logging database, the logging database
and the cleanup of old data on page 254.

Variable for barcode / QR
code

A variable that contains the last incoming text message from the scanner.

COM (serial port)

the table below, you can find the properties you can configure for this communication module type.

Property Description
