Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Property Description

COM port The COM port on which the external device is connected.
Baud Rate The baud rate of the serial connection. Check the manual of the connected device
to know the Baud Rate.

Data bits The information to transmit, usually one of the values below:
 5 for baudot code
 7 for true ASCII
 8 for most kinds of data since this is the size of a byte
Stop bits The stop bits allow the receiving signal hardware to detect the end of a character
and to resynchronize with the character stream.
Parity The party is a method of detecting errors in transmission:
 None :
no parity bit is sent at all.
 Odd :
Counts the given set of bits with value 1, sets the parity bit so the count is odd.
 Even :
Counts the given set of bits with value 1, sets the parity bit so the count is even.
 Mark :
Set the parity bit to 1.
 Space :
Set the parity bit to 0.

Handshake Handshaking is an automated process for negotiation between two entities before
communication is possible.
 None:
No control is used for the handshake
 XOnXOff:
the XON/XOFF software control protocol is used.
 RTS:
Request to send hardware flow control is used.
 RTS/XOnXOff:
Both RTS and XOnXOff software controls are used.
Receive Append Until
Symbol

If unchecked, every incoming message is used to update the selected variable and
spark subsequent components.
If checked, incoming data is concatenated until a newline character appears, even
if this data is spread across multiple messages.

Receive New Line Symbol Select the new line symbol to use for receiving:
 CR LF (\r\n): carriage return + line feed
 CR (\r): carriage return
 LF (\n): line feed
 Custom: specify a new line symbol of your choice

Send Append Symbol If checked, the Send New Line Symbol is appended at the end of a message
when sending.

Send New Line Symbol Select the new line symbol to use for sending.
 CR LF (\r\n): carriage return + line feed
 CR (\r): carriage return
 LF (\n): line feed
 Custom: specify a new line symbol of your choice

Database
The Database communication module is used to communicate with a MySQL, MS SQL Server,
Oracle, Maria DB or SQLite database. A variable is used to represent a query which will be executed

Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

against the database. If the query is a select statement, you can either choose to store the first row of
the result in a number of variables or to store all rows as a JSON array.

Property Description

Name Name of the communication module

and the cleanup of old data on page 254.

type

 INFO
 WARNING
 ERROR

Database Type Database type. Currently supported types are:
 MS SQL Server
 MySQL
 Oracle Database

 Maria DB

Server The name or URL of the server running the database.

User The user who is used to query the database. This user should have the proper
rights to access the table defined below.
Password The password used to authenticate the user with.
Note
You can click the button to make the password youve entered visible and
verify if you havent made any typing mistakes.

Database The name of the database on the server.

In case of SQLite, this should be the path to the database file on the servers
file system.
For example: C:\Arkite\server\mydatabase.db
Shared drives are not supported.

Pick To Light (DMX)
The Pick To Light (DMX) communication module is used to connect DMX lights, either over the Art-
Net ethernet protocol or through an Enttec Open DMX USB interface (SKU 70303). You can then link
your detections to a DMX light, and use the DMX light for operator guidance instead of a projection.
Alternatively, you can also control a DMX light through a Send Communication step.In the table
below, you can find the properties you can configure for this communication module type.

Connectivity

Type Select how you want to connect DMX lights:
 Art-Net: the Art-Net ethernet protocol allows you to control multiple DMX
universes from a single device.
 DMX USB: connect your DMX lights through an Enttec Open DMX USB
interface (SKU 70303). You will need a separate cable for each DMX device.

IP Address Only available if Art-Net is selected in the Type property.
The IP address of the ethernet controller you use to control your DMX lights.
DMX device Only available if DMX USB is selected in the Type property.
The serial number of the Enttec Open DMX USB interface that is linked to the

Local Port The TCP/IP port to use on your workstation.

Important
For the Inter-Workstation communication to work, the communication module needs to be
configured on both workstations. The Local Port on the first workstation needs to be the same
one as the Remote Port on the second workstation, and vice versa.

MQTT
The MQTT communication module is used to communicate through MQTT (Message Queue
Telemetry Transport), a lightweight and flexible network protocol that supports asynchronous
communication between parties. The MQTT protocol defines two types of network entities: a message
broker and a number of clients. An MQTT broker is a server that receives all messages from the
clients and then routes the messages to the appropriate destination clients. Your workstation(s) will
act as MQTT client(s). In the table below, you can find the properties you can configure for this
communication module type.

Property Description

Name Name of the communication module
Note
Next to the Name label, the object ID for the communication module is shown.
You can copy it to use it when working with the Arkite API. For more information
about the Arkite API, refer to chapter 18 The Arkite API on page 281.

Log Table The table name in the logging database in which all incoming and outgoing messages
and exceptions will be logged.
Note
The logging database is configured in the server settings. For more information,
refer to section 13.3 Changing the logging database, the logging database
and the cleanup of old data on page 254.

Variables Variables that will be synced with the MQTT broker. For each variable, the information
below can be configured:
Variable Name of the variable

Topic Information on the broker and the clients are organized in a
hierarchy of topics.
Topic on the MQTT broker where the value will be read from or
written to.

Publish/Subscribe  Publish:
any change to the state of the variable will be sent to the
MQTT broker and stored in the relevant topic.
 Subscribe:
any change to the topic value on the MQTT broker will be
stored in the variables state.
State The current value of the variable.

Broker Address The IP address of the MQTT broker.
Port The port on which to connect to the MQTT broker. The default port for the MQTT
protocol is 1883 , or 8883 when TLS is used.

Use credentials If checked, a username and password are used to authenticate when connecting to
the MQTT broker.
Username The user to connect to the MQTT broker.

Password The password used to authenticate the user with.
Note
You can click the button to make the password youve entered visible and
verify if you havent made any typing mistakes.

Use TLS If checked, the communication is encrypted using the TLS (Transport Layer Security)
protocol.

Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Property Description

Client ID ID that is used to identify the workstation when connecting to the MQTT broker.^ It is
advised to choose something meaningful to you, e.g. the workstation name (assembly
station, packing table...)
In case you dont fill in a client ID, Arkite will randomly generate one.
Note
In some MQTT brokers, you need to configure the client IDs that can connect.
Those MQTT brokers wont accept randomly generated client IDs. Please consult
your MQTT brokers documentation for more information.

Automatic Smart Tool
Settings

If this checkbox is enabled, the required variables for communication with a smart
tool will be generated and configured.
IP Address The IP address of the remove device, for example: 10.0.11.12.

Device Type  When using Atlas Copcos MicroTorque Controller MTF6000, select MTFocus
6000.
 For all other devices, select Generic.
Port The TCP/IP port to use. Default for open protocol communication is 4545.
Start communication
revision

When an open protocol communication actuator is first sparked, a start
communication message will be sent to the controller. This message contains a 3
digit revision. For most controllers, this revision is 001. Check the manual of your
controller to check for divergent revisions.
End communication revision When the module is paused, an end communication message will be sent to the
controller. This message contains a 3 digit revision. For most controllers, this
revision is 001. Check the manual of your controller to check for divergent
revisions.

Stop String Type Every message will be ended by a special ending character. The default value is
null (null character). Other types include a CRLF (carriage return line feed) and #.

Log Keep Alive messages Every incoming, outgoing and exception message will be logged. However, to keep
the connection with the controller open, keep alive messages will be sent (and
received) every ten seconds. In most situations, you dont want to see these
messages cluttering your message stream. However, if you would like to see these
messages, please check this checkbox.

Open Protocol Device Test Before an open protocol device can be used, a parameter set must always be
selected. Provide a parameter set in the text input field (typically consisting of three
digits, e.g. 000, 001, 002....) and click Set Parameter.
Once you have done that:
 Click the Enable Tool button to enable the tool.
 Click the Disable Tool button to disable the tool.
By clicking these buttons, the communication towards the tool can be tested.

Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Once youve configured the open protocol module, you can set up a smart tool that uses the module:
  1. Select the card for the Open Protocol module, click the ... button in the lower-right corner of the
    card and select Add Smart Tool (detection).
Note
Only one tool can be linked to a single Open Protocol module. To use multiple tools, create
multiple Open Protocol modules.
  1. A smart tool linked to the Open Protocol module is created on the Detections tab. Click the toast
    message in the lower-right corner of the screen to navigate to it.
  2. (optional) When using a Validate or Vision license, teach the tool as described in section Teach
    an object, picking bin, tool or virtual button on page 127. This way the system can detect
    when the tool is taken away or placed back.
  3. On the Connectivity tab, select the card for the Open Protocol module, click the ... button in the
    lower-right corner of the card and select Add Activity (detection).
Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. An activity linked to the smart tool you set up in step 5 is created on the Detections tab. Click the
    toast message in the lower-right corner of the screen to navigate to it.
  2. (optional) When using a Validate or Vision license, teach the activity as described in section
    Teach an activity on page 134.
    This way the system can detect when the tool is being used at the desired location.
  3. Add more activities as needed.

about the Arkite API, refer to chapter 18 The Arkite API on page 281.

Log Table The table name in the logging database in which all incoming and outgoing
messages and exceptions will be logged.
Note
The logging database is configured in the server settings. For more information,
refer to section 13.3 Changing the logging database, the logging database
and the cleanup of old data on page 254.

Variables Variables that will be synced with the PLC. For each variable, the information
below can be configured:

Variable Name of the variable
DB Data Block in the PLC where the value will be read from or written
to.

Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Property Description

Data Type Can be any of the following:
 Bit: Boolean value. Can be TRUE or FALSE, 0 or 1
 Byte : bit string of 8 bits.
 Word: bit string of 16 bits.
 DWord: bit string of 32 bits.
 Int:
signed integer with a length of 16 bits. Values can be -32 768 to
+32 767.
 DInt:
signed integer with a length of 32 bits. Values can be -2 147 483
648 to +2 147 483 647.
 Real:
signed floating number with a length of 32 bits. The precision
defined by the IEEE754 standard is stored. Additionally specified
decimals are rounded off.
 LReal:
signed floating number with a length of 64 bits. The precision
defined by the IEEE754 standard is stored. Additionally specified
decimals are rounded off.
 String: ASCII character.
 S7String:
ASCII character string incl. special characters. The length of the
string can be defined, and can contain up to 254 characters.
 S7WString:
Unicode character string. The default length is 254 characters,
but you can define a length up to 16382 characters.
 Timer: contains a timer operation
 Counter: contains a counter operation
 DateTime:
stores date and time information in BCD format (year-month-
day-hour:minute:second:millisecond)
 DateTimeLong:
stores date and time information in a predefined structure (Year-
Month-Day-Hour:Minute:Second.Nanoseconds)

Offset Relative address in the datablock where the value will be read from
or written to. Addresses in a datablock are defined by a byte and a
bit.
 For the data type Bit , use the format byte.bit.
For example, "10.4" will read from or write to bit 4 of byte 10.
 For the data types String or WString , use the pattern
byte.bit[length].
For example, "20.0[100]" will read or write 100 bytes starting
from byte 20. If you dont provide a length, the default length of
the data type will be used.
 For all other data types, use the format byte.
For example: "54" will start reading from or writing to byte 54.
The number of bytes that will be written or read depends on the
length of the data type. In case the data type is dint, the length is
4 bits. Bytes 54 to 57 will be read or written.

I/O Indicates if the variable will be written to or read from the PLC.
State The current value of the variable. Accepted variables depend on
the selected Data Type.

Log
Message

If checked, the sent or received data will be logged in the Message
History.

Note
For more detailed information, consult the documentation of your PLC
programming application.

Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Property Description

S7 Type The type of the connected S7 device.
IP Address The IP address of the connected S7 device.
Rack number The rack number of the connected S7 device. Default value is 0.

Slot number The slot number of the connected S7 device. Default value for S7-200, S7-300 and
S7-400 is 2, S7-1200 and S7-1500 is 1.

Polling rate The interval in ms with which the variables will be synced with the PLC.

Property Description

Name Name of the communication module

Receive variable The variable that will be used to store the received messages.

Encoding Defines how the data being sent or received is represented:
 String: data is interpreted as a text string, using UTF encoding.
 Hex: data is represented in hexadecimal format, where each byte is shown as a two-
digit hex number (0-9, a-f)
Message boundary Defines how the end of a message is determined:
 TCP/IP packet : each TCP packet is interpreted as a different message
 Delimiter : a message ends with a specific character/sequence. For String encoding,
the delimiter is defined in the Delimiter property. For Hex encoding, the delimiter is
0.
 Fixed Length: a message consists of a fixed number of bytes.

Delimiter The delimiter that defines the end of a message:
 Space
 Tab
 New line
 Carriage return
 Carriage return + new line
Only available if String is selected in the Encoding property and Delimiter is selected
in the Message Boundary property. For Hex encoding, the delimiter is 0.

Fixed length (bytes) The message length in bytes.
Only available if Fixed Length is selected in the Message Boundary property.

Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Property Description

Padding character (left) Character that is added on the left of a sent message that is shorter than the defined
fixed length.
Only available if String is selected in the Encoding property and Fixed Length is
selected in the Message Boundary property. For Hex encoding, the padding character
is 0.

Port The TCP port to listen on. The client device should send its messages to this port.
Connection The status of the TCP/IP server and the clients that are connected to it will be listed
here:

7.3.3 Adding a communication module

What?
Before you can start using a communication module, you need to add and configure it in the Arkite
software.

Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Steps
To add a communication module, execute the following steps:
  1. In the Connectivity tab under Communication , click the + button and select the communication
    module you want to add.
A new card for the communication module is added to the list of communication modules.
  1. In the Properties pane, configure the properties for the communication module.
    Note
    The properties that need to be configured depend on the communication module type you have
    added. For an overview of each property and its meaning, refer to section 7.3.2 Communication
    module types on page 189.
    Result
    The communication module has been configured and will immediately start running. Data will be
    received through the communication module. The status icon in the upper right corner of the card
    indicates if the module is correctly configured and running.
Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

For the communication module to send data, you need to add a process step , defining which data to
send. You can also configure a trigger for the communication module to start a process when
receiving data.

7.3.4 Configuring lights for a Pick To Light (DMX) communication module

What
After you have connected a DMX device through a Pick To Light (DMX) communication module, you
can configure different lights on that device by defining which channels to use.
After configuring a light, you can control it by linking it to a detection. This way, you can use the DMX
light for operator guidance instead of a projection. Alternatively, you can also control the light through
a Send Communication process step.

Steps

  1. On the Connectivity tab, click the Configure Lights button in the Properties tab or click Ligths
    and then Configure on the communication module card.
  2. In the Configure Lights window, click the button.
    A light is added with default name L1.
  3. Edit the properties for the DMX Light:
    Property Description
Name Name of the DMX light
Note
Next to the Name label, the object ID for the communication module is shown.
You can copy it to use it when working with the Arkite API. For more information
about the Arkite API, refer to chapter 18 The Arkite API on page 281.

Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Property Description

Universe Only available if you are connecting to the DMX lights over the Art-Net ethernet
protocol, allowing you to control multiple DMX universes, each consisting of 512
channels.
Start Address The first channel on the DMX device that will be used to control the light. By
default, the first unused channel will be selected.
Note
When using Art-Net, channels are within the range 0-511.
When using DMX USB, channels are within the range 1-512.

Number of channels The number of channels^ on the DMX device that will be used to control the light. By
default, 4 channels will be used.
Channel Mapping Depending on the Start Address and the Number of Channels , a table is shown
with a row for each channel. Select what each channel will be used for in the
configuration of an RGB color value and light intensity (Dimmer).
For channels that should not be used, select None.
Max Dimmer Range Configure the value that corresponds to the lights maximum light intensity. By
default 255.

Test your configuration
After configuring your light, you can use each channel using the R, G and B toggle buttons. The light
will emit the corresponding color until the button is pressed again, the window is closed or another
light is selected To test the Dimmer channel, use the slider next to the toggle buttons. Use the Off
button to completely turn off the light manually.

Reset Lights
To reset all lights linked to the Pick To Light (DMX) module to their default value, typically off, click
Lights and then Reset on the communication module.

7.3.5 Configuring a step for the communication module to send data

What?
In order to enable the communication module to send data, you need to configure a process step,
defining when which data will be sent.

Steps

  1. Navigate to the Steps or Processes tab.
Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. Click the New Step button.
  2. Select the Communication subtab, click the communication module you want to wait for and
    select the Send: action from the context menu.
Note
When using Open Protocol communication, you can select the action you want to execute from
the context menu. The correct message will then be preconfigured. The available options are:
  • Enable Tool
  • Disable Tool
  • Select Parameter
  • Select Job
  • Other...: this will allow you to specify your own message
    Before an open protocol device can be used, a parameter set must always be selected. If the tool
    does not react after sending an     Enable Tool message, make sure a parameter set is selected.
    Send a     Select Parameter message first.
    Note
    When using Pick To Light (DMX) communication, you can select the light you want to control from
    the context menu. In most use cases, you will control a DMX light by linking it to a detection. For
    more information, refer to section     5.5 Adding detections on page 121.
    Note
    Apart from the communication modules you have added in the Connectivity tab, you can also
    select a     Projector display that is available in the Displays section of the Connectivity tab here.
  1. Configure the properties for the step.
    The properties that need to be configured depend on the communication module type. You can
    find an overview of properties per communication module type below. By clicking the Comment
Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

icon next to the Name property, you can add a few words of explanation regarding the use of the
step.

all rows that are returned are stored in a JSON array, with a maximum of 10 000

only the first row in the result is taken into account. For every column in the

Variables for Query The variables you specify here are encoded in the query part of the URL. If the
Variables for Query list contains one element variableName the request could
look like this:
http://myservice/logger?variableName=variableValue
Resulting URL The requests that results from the contents of the URL and Variable for Query
properties.

Request Type The HTTP request type.
You can select one of the values below:
 Get:
this method is used to retrieve the representation of a resource
 Post:
this method is used to create new resources
 Put:
this method is typically used to update capabilities of a resource. The request
body contains the newly-updated representation of the original resource.
 Patch:
this method is typically used to modify capabilities of a resource. The request
body contains the changes to the resource, not the complete resource.
 Delete :
this method is used to delete a resource identified by a URI

Body Content Type Only visible when the Request Type is Post, Put or Patch.
Determines the content type of the body. There are currently two options:
 Raw (=default option):
You can specify the body of the request in the Raw Body Content property.
 FormData:
The variable names and their current states you specify in the Variables for
Form Data property will be sent in FormData format.
Variables for Form Data When the Body Content Type is FormData , the variables you specify here are
encoded in the body of the request in FormData format.

Content Type When Body Content Type is Raw , the content type of the raw data should be
specified. By default, this is application/json

 Open Protocol
Property Description

Header Depending on the option you have selected in the context menu when adding the
process step, the header will be prefilled with the Open Protocol message that is
required to complete the action of your choice:
 Enable Tool: 00200043 (Generic) / 0023022500100000000 008 (MTFocus 6000)
 Disable Tool: 00200042 (Generic) / 0023022400100000000 008 (MTFocus
6000)
 Select Parameter: 00230018001 (Generic and MTFocus 6000)
 Select Job: 00220038001 (Generic and MTFocus 6000)
 Other...: the header remains empty, you can specify a message yourself.
Note
Before an open protocol device can be used, a parameter set must always be
selected. If the tool does not react after sending an Enable Tool message,
make sure a parameter set is selected. Send a Select Parameter message
first.
To have a full overview of all message types that are supported by Open Protocol,
you can consult the Open Protocol specification documents embedded below.

Generic
MTFocus 6000

Open Protocol messages consist of 20 digits (for example.
00200001000000000000 for communication start).
 Digit 1  4: Length
 Digit 5  8: MID
 Digit 9  11: Revision
 Digit 12: No ack flag
 Digit 13  14: Station ID
 Digit 15  16: Spindle ID
 Digit 17  20: Spare
Note
If the header is less than 20 digits, it will be padded with spaces until it contains
20 digits before being sent.
If the header is more than 20 digits, the excess will be considered data.

Data Insert the data you want to be appended to the header. Together with the ending
character, this will be the full message to be sent to the controller.
To insert dynamic content, click the icon at the location where you want to
include the content and select the variable containing the dynamic content.
Alternatively, you can also type the variable name between double braces, i.e.
{{Variable name}}.
Tip
For long texts, click the icon to enlarge the text box.
Note
The ending character is defined by the property Stop String Type configured in
the communication module. Refer to section Open Protocol on 197 for more
information.

Connectivity

 Projector
Property Description

Projector Command The commands below can be sent to the projector:
 Power On: turns on the projector
 Power Off: turns off the projector
 Switch To VGA: switches the active input of the projector to VGA
 Switch To HDMI1: switches the active input of the projector to HDMI1
 Switch To HDMI2: switches the active input of the projector to HDMI2
 Mute On: mutes the video and audio of the projector
 Mute Off: stops muting the video and audio of the projector
 Get Current State: returns the (power) state of the projector
 Get Current Input: returns the active input of the projector
 Get Error Code: returns the error code of the projector (returns 000000 when
there is no error)
 Get Lamp Hours: returns the number of hours the projector has been active

Variable for answer The variable in which the responses of the projector will be stored.

 TCP/IP Server

content and select the variable containing the dynamic content. Alternatively, you
can also type the variable name between double braces, i.e. {{Variable name}}.
Tip
For long texts, click the icon to enlarge the text box.

and select the variable containing the dynamic content. Alternatively, you can also
type the variable name between double braces, i.e. {{Variable name}}.

7.3.6 Configuring a step to wait for the receival of data from the

communication module

What?
You can add a step in your job or process that pauses your job or process until data is received from a
communication module. For example, you can configure the process to wait for a barcode being
scanned.

Steps

  1. Navigate to the Steps or Processes tab.
  2. Click the New Step button.
  3. Select the Communication subtab, click the communication module you want to wait for and
    select the Wait for... action from the context menu.
Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. Configure the properties for the step.
    The properties that need to be configured depend on the communication module type. You can
    find an overview of properties per communication module type below. By clicking the Comment
    icon next to the Name property, you can add a few words of explanation regarding the use of the
    step.
 Open Protocol
Property Description

MID to filter on The MID (which is character 5 to 8 of the message header) to filter the messages
on.
If this field is filled in, only messages with a matching MID will be captured and the
job or process will only continue when the matching MID is received.
If this field is left empty, all messages will be captured. The process will continue
whenever a message is received.
Variable for message The variable that will be used to store the received messages.

 Inter-Workstation
Property Description

Variables When the variable(s) you indicate here are received from the other workstation, the
job or process will continue.
Check the All Variables checkbox to continue the job or process when receiving
any variable.
For the modules below, no additional properties need to be configured. The job or process will
continue as soon as any message is received on the corresponding communication module:
 Barcode Scanner
 COM (serial port)

 Modbus TCP
 TCP/IP Server
 TCP/IP Client

 MQTT
 S7 PLC

Result
The process or job has been configured to wait for the receival of data from the communication
module.
On the Connectivity tab, the incoming communication will be listed in the Associated objects for the
communication module. Click the ... button in the lower-right corner of the card and select Associated
objects.

7.3.7 Configuring a trigger for the communication module to start a

process when receiving data

What?
You can configure a process to start when data is received through the communication module you
have added. In order to do so, you need to configure a communication trigger.

Steps

  1. On the Processes tab, select the process you want to trigger by the receival of communication.
  2. In the Properties pane, under Start by trigger , click the button.
  3. Select Receive Communication.
  4. Under Trigger Properties , select the module you want to configure as a trigger from the
    Communication Module dropdown list.
  5. Configure the properties for the trigger.
    The properties that need to be configured depend on the communication module type. You can
    find an overview of properties per communication module type below.
    Inter-Workstation
    Property Description
Variables The variables that are going to be received.
Check the All Variables checkbox to send all variables.

 Modbus TCP
Property Description

Variable The variable that will be used to store the received messages.
Address Type The object type of the read action. It is possible to read:
 Discrete inputs: read-only entity with a size of 1 bit (ON/OFF)
 Coils : read-write entity with a size of 1 bit (ON/OFF)
 Input registers: read-only entity with a size of 16 bits (0-65 535)
 Holding registers: read-write entity with a size of 16 bits (0-65 535)

Address The address of the object from which will be read.
The process will be started when a message is received from the address specified
here, with the correct type.

 Open Protocol
Property Description

MID to filter on The MID (which is character 5 to 8 of the message header) to filter the messages
on.
If this field is filled in, only messages with a matching MID will be captured and the
process will only be started when the matching MID is received.
If this field is left empty, all messages will be captured. The process will started
whenever a message is received.

Variable The variable that will be used to store the received messages.

7.3.8 Following up on the communication that has been exchanged

What?
Once you have correctly set up the communication module and the associated triggers or actuators,
you can follow up on the exchanged information.

How to follow up on exchanged information
On the Connectivity tab, the latest outgoing and incoming communication will be listed in the
Messages... field on the card for the communication module.

Three types of messages can appear:

 IN: Incoming messages
 OUT: Outgoing messages
 ERROR: Error messages, specifying what is wrong
To view more messages, click the Message Log button.

 To delete a communication module, select it, click the ... button in the lower-right corner of the

The message history is copied to your clipboard.
 To clear a communication modules message history, select it, click the ... button in the lower-right

7.4 Sensors.............................................................................................................

What?
The Sensors section in the Connectivity tab manages the sensors that are used in the project.
Whenever a sensor is connected, it is automatically added to the list.
The items in the list show the sensors that are used in the project.
On a typical workstation with a Validate license, two sensors appear: the Arkite 3D sensor, a time-of-
flight sensor that has the ability to measure both distance and infrared, and an RGB camera for
regular color images.
For making RGB product snapshots, we recommend using a Daheng RGB sensor.
Webcams are also supported: simply plug it into an available USB port, and it appears in the list.
On a typical workstation with a Vision license, a third sensor appears: the Arkite Vision sensor.
If sensors are at some point not available, they remain to be part of the project. For example, if a
project is edited on a laptop, the sensors are not connected but remain part of the project. This allows
to continue editing without having an actual sensor connected.

Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Note
The Arkite 3D and Arkite Vision sensors, the Daheng RGB sensor and webcams are detected by
default when connected. You can enable a few other sensor types by clicking the button.
However, these other types of sensor are all experimental. If you want to use one of them, please
contact support@arkite.com to verify which features are supported.

Specifying Sensor Serial Number
If a project uses multiple sensors of the same type, you have to specify their serial number, so the
software knows without ambiguity which connected sensor corresponds to which logical sensor of the
project.
For example, if two Daheng RGB sensors are used to make product snapshots, and one is called Left
RGB sensor and the other is called Right RGB sensor, you have to specify which serial number
corresponds to the Left RGB sensor, and do the same for the right camera. You have to specify this
for every unit that uses the project, as the serial numbers of the respective sensors will be different.
Whenever action is required, a warning appears in the status bar.
To specify the sensor serial number, select the sensor card. In the Properties pane, select the correct
serial number in the Specified Serial dropdown list. In the Name field, you can specify a meaningful
name for the sensor.

Note
In a typical case, where only one sensor of a certain type is used, there is no need to specify the
serial numbers and the default <Automatic> can be left untouched. The software will
automatically use the attached sensor of the same type.

Setting the exposure time for a Daheng RGB sensor
When connecting a Daheng RGB sensor, the exposure time is set by default to 30 milliseconds.
To set another exposure time, select the sensor card. In the Properties pane under Exposure ,
uncheck the Automatic checkbox and in the Exposure time (ms) property, set the exposure time of
your choice.

Connectivity

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Removing a sensor
To remove a sensor, click the ... button in the lower-right corner of the senors card and select Delete.

An example use case is when an external webcam was required in a project was, which was at one
point connected and hence a webcam sensor appeared in the list. If, later on, the webcam is no longer
needed, it can be permanently removed.

Viewing the sensor stream
To view images from the sensor on your screen, click the View Stream button in the sensor card.

Experience levels

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

8. Experience levels

8.1 About experience levels

The Experience level functionality allows you to customize your project and change its behavior
based on the operators level of experience:

 When the Experience Level functionality is disabled, the project behavior will be the same for all
operators.
 When the Experience Level functionality is enabled, by default three operator experience levels
become available.
Depending on the experience level, you can customize:
 Detection settings (Validate and Vision license only)
 Projection settings
 Display of visualizations

8.2 Managing experience levels

Enabling experience levels
To enable the Experience level functionality, execute the steps below:
  1. In the ribbon, click the Experience Level button.
The Experience Level window opens.
  1. Check the Experience levels enabled checkbox.
The Experience level functionality is enabled. The functionality in the Experience Level window
becomes available.

Available experience levels
By default, three experience levels are available:
 Level 1: Training
 Level 2: Basic

 Level 3: Advanced
After enabling the Experience level functionality, by default level 1 will be used.

Experience levels

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Modifying experience level names
To change the name for an experience level, update its label in the Experience Level window under
Level names. The experience level name will be updated throughout the application.

Experience level options
In the Experience Level window under Options , you can specify whether:
 the selected experience level should be retained after restarting the project.
 the experience level should be reset to the default Level 1 every time the project is restarted.

8.3 Experience level settings

Detection settings (Validate and Vision license only)
For every detection in your project, there are time threshold properties that define for how long an
object needs to be within (ON) or outside (OFF) the range defined in the fill rate properties to change
detection state.
In the Experience Level window under Detection Settings , you can set a percentage of these time
thresholds that will be used for every specific experience level.
By default, these percentages are set to:
 100% for level 1
 50% for level 2

 20% for level 3

This means that for a detection with a time threshold of 40 ms, the following thresholds will be used for
each specific level:

 40 ms for level 1

Experience levels

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

 20 ms for level 2
 8 ms for level 3
You can change the percentages for every level as required. It is also possible to overrule these
default percentages for a specific detection. For more information, refer to section 5.6.5 Finetune a
detection on page 141.

Projection settings
In the Experience Level window under Projection Settings , you can customize the projection
settings independently for each experience level.
The options are:

 For the current step in your process:
 ON: a projection will be shown
 ON BLINK: a projection will be shown and it will blink
 OFF: no projection will be shown
 For errors during your process (Validate and Vision license only):
 ERROR: a projection will be shown

 ERROR BLINK: a projection will be shown and it will blink
 OFF: no projection will be shown

Example
In a training situations for novice users, you may choose to use blinking projections for the Current
Step (ON BLINK) for Level 1. Blinking projections attract attention more quickly but can also
quickly become distracting or irritating for an operator. Therefore, we recommend using them only
in training scenarios.
Note
To change the colors of these projections, click the Color Templates button in the ribbon and
select the Detection colors template. There you can update the colors for the projection settings
mentioned above. For more information, refer to section 15.2 The Detection Colors template on
page 266.

Experience levels

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Display of visualizations
In the Properties of a visualization, there is a new Experience Level property.

This way, you can define whether the visualization will be displayed for a specific experience level or
not. By default, every visualization is shown for all experience levels.
Example
You can choose to show text instructions to users with Level 1 (Training) or Level 2 (Basic) but
hide them for users with Level 3 (Advanced) , since there is no real added value for those users.
Note
For more information on the properties of a visualization, refer to sections 4.4.1 Visualization
types on page 77 and 4.4.2 Visualization properties on page 78 ..

8.4 Selecting the experience level

Selection by the project administrator
To change the experience level in the Arkite software, execute the steps below:
  1. In the ribbon, click the Experience Level button.
The Experience Level window opens.
  1. Make sure the Experience levels enabled checkbox is checked.
  2. Click the Change current level... button.
    The Variables window opens. The variable Experience Level is selected.
Experience levels

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. Change the value in the column Current State to the experience level of your choice (1, 2 or 3).
The experience level has been changed.

Selection by the operator
By default, an Arkite project contains a Menu Bar on the Screen display, in which the operator can
select the experience level from a dropdown list if the feature is enabled.

Note
In projects made in a software version before 2025.1, you will still need to add the menu bar
(typically on the master).

Variables

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

9. Variables.....................................................................................................................

9.1 About variables

Variables are data items that can have different values or states during your assembly process.
Some variables are automatically generated by the Arkite software, for example detection and system
variables. Other variables are created by the user.
The state of a variable can be used to log information or to trigger something in the process.
In the Variables overview, you can see:

 All project-wide variables, i.e. variables that are available across jobs
 All job-specific variables for the currently selected job
Within each section, variables are grouped per variable type.

9.2 Variable types

In the table below, you can find a list of available variable types:

Detection type Description

Detection variables
(Validate and Vision
license only)

Variables generated by the Arkite software for every detection that is added.
Detection variables can be Project-Wide variables or Job-Specific , depending on the
detection type.
 For every detection, there is a variable that indicates if the detection is present (ON) or
not (OFF).
 For every detection, there is an occluder_ variable that indicates if the detection is
occluded (ON) or not (OFF).
 For every detection, there is a Vis_ variable that indicates whether visualizations for
the detection are projected or not
 For every detection, there is a Sb_ variable that indicates whether shadowboards for
the detection are projected or not
 For every detection, there are PositionX_ and PositionY_ variables that indicate the
position of the detection
 For every detection, there is an OrientationAngle_ variable that indicates the
orientation of the detection
 For every detection, there are VisPositionError_ and VisOrientationError _ variables
that indicate whether error visualizations for the position or orientation of the detection
are projected or not
 For every picking bin, there is a pick_ variable that indicates whether material is being
picked from the picking bin (ON) or not (OFF).
 For every picking bin, there is a _material variable that indicates the material that is
linked to the picking bin

Instruction variables Variables generated by the Arkite^ software^ for displaying instructions. Instruction
variables are Project-Wide variables:
 Text instructions variable, containing the currently displayed text instruction
 Image instructions variable, containing the currently displayed image instruction
 Error instructions variable, containing the currently displayed error message (in case of
a Quality Check or Object with Quality Check)

9.4 Watching variables

About Watches
In the Watches panel, you can add a number of variables you want to keep track of. It shows the
variable name along with its current state. This way, you can easily make a selection of variables to
monitor, and put them together in a comprehensive overview.

Opening and closing the Watches panel
To open or close the Watches panel, click Watches in the ribbon.

The Watches panel will open in the right side of the screen, as a second tab next to the Properties
panel.

Adding and removing variables to the Watches panel
Click the + icon to add a variable and its state to the Watches panel.
Select a variable and click the  icon to remove it from the Watches panel, or right-click the variable
and select Remove.

and select Add Watch.

10. Recordings (Validate and Vision license only)

10.1 About recording

The Arkite software allows you to record the sensor stream. These recordings can be sent to Arkite for
support, or you can use them to add detections from the comfort of your desk.

10.2 Creating recordings

You can create recordings in several ways:

Record manually

  1. In the ribbon, click Recordings.
The Recordings panel will open in the right side of the screen, as a second tab next to the
Properties panel.
  1. Click Record to start the recording.
Note
To change the sensor(s) that is/are recorded, click the Sensors menu and select the sensor(s) of
your choice.
  1. Perform the activities you want to record.
  2. Click the Record button again to stop the recording.
Recordings (Validate and Vision license only)

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. Provide a name for your recording and click OK.
Your recording is saved.

Auto Record

  1. In the ribbon, click Recordings.
The Recordings panel will open in the right side of the screen, as a second tab next to the
Properties panel.
  1. Click the Auto Record button.
A recording is made for every completed step involving a detection. Nothing is recorded during
idle time.
  1. Click the Auto Record button again to deactivate auto recording.

10.3 Managing recordings

In the ribbon, click Recordings.

Recordings (Validate and Vision license only)

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

The Recordings panel will open in the right side of the screen, as a second tab next to the Properties
panel.

Right-click a recording and select Delete or click the button to delete it.
To export the recordings to a .hrec file, click the button.
To import a recording from another project, click the button and select the .hrec file of your choice.

10.4 Using recordings

Recordings can be used by Arkite for troubleshooting and support.
You can also use recordings yourself, for example for adding detections while you are not at the
workbench.
To do this, execute the following steps:
  1. At the workbench, make a recording of the sensor stream and make sure to remove all objects,
    tools and picking bins and put them back at the location of your choice one by one.
    Perform all activities for which you want to create a detection.
  2. Open the project on your pc.
    Make sure you also import the recording.
  3. In the ribbon, click Recordings.
The Recordings panel will open in the right side of the screen, as a second tab next to the
Properties panel.

Recordings (Validate and Vision license only)

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. Select the recording of your choice and click the Play button.
The recording starts to play in the Teaching subtab of the Detections tab

You can drag the round handles to set the start and end time of the recording and use the arrow
marker to select the current time.
Use the buttons to play and pause the recording, to browse through the recording frame by frame
or to trim the recording.

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

    pausing the recording at a frame where the object is not at its place and take a Without
    object snapshot
    pausing the recording at a frame where the object is at its place and take a With object

  2. To return to the live feed of the sensor, click the Switch to live button in the Recordings pane.
Server management

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

11. Server management....................................................................................................

11.1 About server management

The Arkite software is split in a workstation and a server component. The server, containing all data
and resources for multiple clients and projects, should preferably run on a separate system to obtain
higher security, maintainability and data integrity.
From within the software on any workstation connected to the server, you can consult an overview of
all workstations on that server, manage licenses and manage backups.

11.2 Connecting to a server

What?
When opening the Arkite software on a workstation the first time, you need to specify to which server
you want to connect. Afterwards, the system automatically connects to that server again when starting
the software. At all times however, you can connect to a different server.

How to connect to a different server

  1. In the top bar, click the [server] button and then Switch Server..
The Server Connection Settings popup appears.
  1. In the Server URL or IP field, fill in the URL or IP address of the server.
  2. Click the Apply Settings and Restart button.
Server management

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

11.3 Workstation overview

What?
From any workstation connected to the server, you can consult information about all workstations that
are connected to the same server, or have been connected to it in the past.

Overview of workstations connected to the server
To consult the overview of workstations, click Menu and then Workstations.

In the overview table, you can see for every connected workstation:
 the workstations Name.
The name can be changed by clicking in the cell and entering a new name.

 the workstations IP address

 Vision (= with Arkite 3D sensor and with Arkite Vision Sensor)

 Validate (= with Arkite 3D sensor)
 Guide (= without sensor)
 none:
in this case, the workstation is an editor. It can be used to prepare and configure projects, but
not to run them. For testing purposes, you will be able to run your project for a maximum of 15
minutes.
Note
Workstations with an invalid license, for example a license that is only valid for a previous software
version, are marked in red.

 the Software version that is running on the workstation.
A warning sign is displayed when the software version is not the same as the server software
version.

 The user hat is logged in on the workstation

 The workstations up-time , i.e. the time it has been connected to the server
 The name of the project that is currently loaded on the workstation

 The time this project was loaded on the workstation
 Vision Ready : indicates if the workstation is ready to be used with an Arkite Vision license.
 Host IDs : ID that is required to make the workstation Vision Ready.

If you have a Vision license, but your workstations are not Vision Ready yet, follow the steps

 The workstation id

The workstation from which the overview is consulted is displayed in bold.

shown mentioning how long ago the workstation disconnected from the server. Workstations that are
displayed in gray can be removed from the overview by selecting them and clicking Delete
Workstation.

11.4 Managing licenses.............................................................................................

What?
When using the workstation for the first time, you need to provide a server License Key. A license key
is valid for a particular number of workstations. From the application, you can manage which
workstations are using the license.

How to consult licenses
To consult licenses, click Menu , then Server and then Settings.
Under Server License , you can see an overview of the license key(s) used for the server, their validity
period, the number of workstations that can use the license and the workstations that are currently
using the license.
In the example below, the Guide , Validate and Vision license keys can all be used for a maximum of
ten workstations is available on the server. For the Vision license, 6 out of 10 slots are used, while for
the Guide license, one slot is used by ARKITE-TRAINING- 4.

Note
A license that is no longer valid or not valid yet is marked in red. In the example below, the license
is only valid from 1/1/2026 (screenshot taken in October 2025).

Server management

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

How to add a license key
You can use several license keys on the same server.
To add a new Server License Key :
  1. Click the Add License button.
  2. In the Add License Key window, in the License Key field fill in your license key or click the ...
    button to select the file containing your license key.
  3. Click Verify.
The details and validity date of your license is displayed.

Server management

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. Check the I agree to the end user license agreement checkbox.
An OK button will appear.
  1. Click OK to confirm.
The license key is added to the overview.

How to manage workstations
To manage the workstations on which the license key is used:

Server management

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. Select the license key and click the Manage Workstations for license button.
  2. In the Manage workstations for this license window:
    Check the checkbox(es) in the License column for the workstation(s) on which you want to
    use the license
    Uncheck the checkbox(es) in the License column for the workstation(s) on which you no
    longer want to use the license
  3. Click Close to apply your changes.
    Note
    • If you have a Vision license, you will only be able to add workstations to it that are Vision
      Ready. If your workstations are not Vision Ready yet, follow the steps described in the
      procedure How to make your workstation Vision Ready (available on the customer drive).
      The number of workstations you can make Vision Ready is limited to the number of
      workstations for which you have bought a Vision license. If you already have reached this
      number, your request will be denied.
    • Workstations for which you have removed the license will lose the license after they have
      rebooted.
Server management

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  • Workstations that are connected to the server but are not assigned to a license will function as
    an editor. You will be able to prepare and configure projects on them, but you cannot use
    them to run a project. For testing purposes, you will be able to run your project for a maximum
    of 15 minutes.
How to renew a license key
Between three and two months before your license expires, you will receive a quotation from Arkite for
the renewal of your contract. Once you have placed the purchase order, you will receive a new license
key. You can then add this new license key as described above, without assigning any workstations to
it yet.
Once your license key expires, the system will automatically check if another valid, comparable
license key with open slots is available. If there is, it will automatically transfer the workstations to the
new license key.

How to remove a license key
To remove a Server License Key, right-click the license and select Remove.

11.5 Managing server backups..................................................................................

What?
Every five minutes, a backup of the server databases is taken (provided there have been any changes
during this timeframe). The 10 most recent backups are always available. Additionally, all backups that
were created right before a server version upgrade also remain available, as well as a selection of
backups from the past. Other backups are removed automatically. You can consult all available
backups and restore a previous version if required.

How to consult server backups
To consult server backups, click Menu , then Server and then Backups.
An overview of all available backups is shown.

For every backup, the information below is displayed:
 The backups creation date
 The software version with which the backup was created

 Comments regarding the backup.
You can add a comment for a backup by clicking in the corresponding cell in the Comments
column and start typing.

Server management

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

 The backups size

How to create a server backup
While you are working on your project, the system automatically takes a backup every five minutes.
Additionally, you can also create a backup yourself at any time.
To do so, click the New backup button on top of the backup overview.

How to restore a server backup
In case of issues, for example a corrupted database, you can put a previous version of your server
database back in place by restoring a backup.
To do so , select the backup and click the Restore button.

Warning
  • Server backups are backups of the entire server database. Restoring a server backup affects
    all versions of all projects on all workstations connected to the server. All workstations will
    need to restart their running project after the restore.
  • Resources, such as image files, are not part of the server backups. This means that when you
    are restoring a server backup in which a resource file is used that has been removed from the
    project since, this resource file will no longer be available. An error message will be shown to
    inform you about the missing file(s).
How to delete a server backup
Older backups are automatically deleted by the system. Additionally, you can also delete server
backups yourself.
To do so , right-click the backup and select Delete.

Server management

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

11.6 Cleaning up server resources

What?
When your disk is (almost) full, a clean up mechanism will remove all unused resources (e.g. image
files). You an also trigger this mechanism yourself and free up disk space in this way.

Steps

  1. Click Menu and then Server.
  2. Under Resources , click the Clean and optimize server data button.
Result
 Unused resources such as image files will be removed.
 The server database will be compacted and defragmented.

Dashboarding

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

12. Dashboarding

12.1 About dashboarding

Dashboarding provides you with insights on various aspects of your assembly process and the status
of your system through a graphical representation of data.

12.2 Consulting dashboards

To consult dashboards, click Menu and then Dashboards.
The dashboards below are currently available in the Arkite software:
 Workstation status:
provides you with information on the current status of each workstation that is connected to your
server. Only workstations with a license are shown.
 Job output:
provides you with information on the number of jobs that have been executed during a specific
period.
 Cycle Times:
provides you with information on the time the execution of a job has taken.
 Current Step Duration:
provides you with real-time information about the current assembly on the workstations connected
to your server. Only workstations with a license are shown.
Note
A lot more information concerning assembly is logged. You can use those to easily create your
own dashboards in a dedicated tool.

12.3 Available dashboards

Workstation status

The workstation status dashboard provides you with information on the current status of each
workstation connected to your server. Only workstations with a valid license are shown. In other
words, editors are not displayed in the overview.

Dashboarding

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Each workstation is represented by a circle and can have four different colors:
 Green:
the workstation is online, and a project is loaded.
 Orange:
the workstation is online, but currently no project is loaded.
 Red:
the workstation is online, but its software version does not match the software version on the
server. It is not possible to load a project
 Gray:
the workstation is currently not connected to the server.
Tip
When you hover over a circle with your mouse, more information on the status and the
workstations license type is displayed in a tool tip.

Current step duration
The Current Step Duration dashboard provides you with real-time information about the current
assembly on the workstations connected to your server. For each workstation with a license, the
dashboard shows the duration of the step that is currently executed and the nine previous steps. Both
job steps and process steps are taken into account. Steps without operator interaction are ignored.

Dashboarding

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

In the dropdown list above the dashboard, you can select the workstation for which you want to see
the step duration.
For every step, you can see:
 The average duration of that step. The average is calculated based on the last 30 executions of
that step. Outliers are not taken into account.

 The duration in seconds of the last time the step has been executed (or for the current step: the
ongoing duration).
In case the duration deviates significantly from the average, the bar for that step is shown in red.
If the deviation from the averages is within range, the bar for that step is shown in green.
Tip
When you hover over a circle with your mouse, the step name and the exact duration and average
duration are displayed in a tool tip.

Job Output
The Job Output dashboard provides you with information on the number of jobs that have been
executed during a specific period.

Click the 1 day button to display the data for the last 24 hours. Data are split per hour.
Click the 1 month button to display the data for the last month. Data are split per day.
Click the 1 year button to display the data for the last 12 months. Data are split per week.
In the Jobs dropdown list, you can select which jobs and job variants you want to see. By default, all
jobs that have been executed on a workstation connected to your server are shown.

 When the Group variants/options checkbox is checked, the data for all job variants and options
is aggregated and one bar per job will be shown.

Dashboarding

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

 When the Group variants/options checkbox is not checked, data will be rendered separately for
each job variant or combination of job options.

Note
  • Click the Refresh button to update the dashboard with the latest data.
  • If you still have data from before the introduction of jobs in the Arkite software, you can show
    these data by selecting PRODUCT_LOG in the Based on dropdown list.
  • When you hover over the graph with your mouse, the exact numbers for each bar in the graph
    are displayed in a tool tip.
Cycle Times
The Cycle Times dashboard provides you with information on the time the execution of a job has
taken. By default, the last 10 executions of a job are shown. Only the last 30 days are taken into
account.

In the Jobs dropdown list, you can select which jobs and job variants you want to see. By default, all
jobs that have been executed on a workstation connected to your server are shown.
 When the Group variants/options checkbox is checked, the data for all job variants and options
is aggregated and one line per job will be shown.
 When the Group variants/options checkbox is not checked, data will be rendered separately for
each job variant or combination of job options.
In the Workstations dropdown list, you can select for which workstations you want to see the cycle
times. By default, data for all workstations connected to your server are shown.

Dashboarding

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

 When the Group Workstations checkbox is checked, one line for each job (variant) will be
shown. You will see the last cycle times for the job (variant), but you wont see on which
workstation these assemblies have taken place.
 When the Group Workstations checkbox is not checked, a separate line for every workstation
will be shown for each job (variant). This allows you to compare cycle times between workstations
for the same job (variant).
In the Number of Cycles dropdown list, you can select how many cycles are shown in the graph.
When the Trendline checkbox is checked, for each job (variant) or job (variant)/workstation
combination a moving average is shown.
When the Expected Cycle Time checkbox is checked, for each job (variant) the expected cycle time
is shown. You can set the expected cycle time in the properties of a job or job variant.
Note
  • Click the Refresh button to update the dashboard with the latest data.
  • If you still have data from before the introduction of jobs in the Arkite software, you can show
    these data by selecting PRODUCT_LOG in the Based on dropdown list.
  • When you hover over the graph with your mouse, the exact numbers for each line in the graph
    are displayed in a tool tip.

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

13. Logging

13.1 About logging

The server contains a database in which information about the platform and its projects are logged.
Logging can be used to troubleshoot or reproduce issues, or to provide you with insights on various
aspects of your assembly process and the status of your system through a graphical representation of
data in dashboards.
A lot of information is logged by default. Additionally, you can also add logging yourself

13.2 Consulting log tables in the Arkite software

To consult the log tables, click the Log Tables button in the ribbon.

The Log Tables window appears.

In the Log Table dropdown list, select the table you want to consult. By default, the log tables below
are available:

Log table Description

GLOBAL_LOG Records are logged for error messages and default actions.
Note
To change the default actions that are logged, refer to section 13.4 Changing
logging settings on page 256.

HEARTBEAT Every 10 seconds, a record is logged when the workstation is online.
STEP_LOG A record is logged for every job step that is executed. You can also add logging for
process steps here. To do so, navigate to the Processes t ab and select the process of
your choice. In the Properties pane, check the Log Steps checkbox.

Logging

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Log table Description

AUDIT_LOG Records are logged for:
 Project creation and deletion
 Any changes to versioning (creating, approving, rejecting, ...)
 Any changes to users and roles
 Maintenance actions

API_LOG A record is logged for every communication with the Arkite API.

JOB_LOG A record is logged every time a job is started, finished or cancelled before its finished.^
The records in this table are used for generating the Job Output and Cycle Time
dashboards.
Note
For more information about dashboarding, refer to chapter 12 Dashboarding on
page 248.

COMMUNICATION Default log table for all communication modules in the project.
A record is logged for every incoming and outgoing message, as well as error messages
related to the communication module.
Note
For more information about communication modules, refer to section 7.3
Communication modules on page 188.

Click Refresh to update the information in the log table.
Click the icon to define which columns from the log table you want to display.
Click Clear Table to remove the records from a log table.

Warning
This action cannot be undone.

13.3 Changing the logging database, the logging

database and the cleanup of old data

To change the logging database and/or the logging database type, execute the steps below:
  1. Click Menu.
  2. Click Server and then Settings.
Logging

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. Under Logging , select the Database Type and enter the Database Connection String.
Note
  • Using MySQL may result in performance issues due to the workload involved. We recommend
    to use MariaDB instead.
  • When using SQLite, specify a path on the server, for example C:\Arkite\server\someDb.db.
    Shared drives are not supported.
  1. Click Test Connection to verify your configuration.
By default, 10 million rows per table are stored. If the number of rows exceeds this threshold, the
oldest rows are cleaned up automatically. You can set a different number of rows between 10 000 and
10 million, or a number of days to keep old data.

Note
You can also disable the automatic clean up mechanism, but be aware that in that case logs keep
on growing and you will run out of disk space eventually.

Logging

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

13.4 Changing logging settings

What?
You can change the default actions that are logged in the Global_LOG table and the steps that are
logged in the STEP_LOG table.

For the GLOBAL_LOG table

  1. Click the Log Tables button in the ribbon.
The Log Tables window appears.
  1. In the Log Table dropdown list, select the Global_LOG table.
  2. Click the button.
Logging

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. Check the checkboxes for the actions you want to log in the Global_LOG database.
  2. Click Close.
For the STEP_LOG table
To add logging for the steps of particular process:
  1. Navigate to the Processes tab.
  2. Select a process.
  3. In the Properties pane, check the Log Steps checkbox.

13.5 Adding logging yourself

Add a Variable Logger step
At any point in your process or job, you can add a step that logs the state of one or more variables:
  1. Navigate to the Steps or Processes tab.
  2. Click the New Step button.
Logging

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. Select the Variables subtab and click Variable Logger.
  2. In the Properties pane, add the variables for which you want to log the state and specify the Log
    Table.
Configure logging for a communication module
When configuring a communication module, you can specify a log table in which all incoming and
outgoing messages and exceptions will be logged. Specify the log table of your choice in the Log
Table property of the communication module.

13.6 Exporting log data

What?
Log data can be exported to a csv file for further analysis in Microsoft Excel for example.

Steps

  1. Click the Log Tables button in the ribbon.
Logging

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

The Log Tables window appears.

  2. Click the Export to CSV button.
  3. In the Export CSV window, indicate the number of rows you want to export or check the Export
    all rows checkbox to export everything.
Note
If you select a number of rows, the most recent records in the database will always be exported.
  1. Click Export.
  2. In the Export CSV window, navigate to the folder of your choice and click Save.
    The selected table is exported to the directory of your choice.
