14. Images

14.1 About images

On several locations in the Arkite software, images and videos can be used, for example:
 Shadowboards for an object or tool
 Images linked to a detection
These are projected on the workbench or shown on the screen when the detection is active.
 Image instructions linked to a process step
These are projected on the workbench or shown on the screen when the process step is active.

 Images linked to a material
These are displayed as an icon for picking bins containing this material
 ...

Project-Wide versus Job-Specific images
Images can be project-wide or job-specific.
Project-wide images can be used in every job in your project, while job-specific images can be used in
one job only, and will only be visible if that job is selected.

14.2 Managing images

Adding images or videos

  1. In the ribbon, click the Images button.
The Images window appears.
  1. To add a project-wide image, select the Project-Wide group.
    To add a job-specific image, first select the relevant job in the ribbon and then select the Job -
    Specific group.
Images

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. Click the New button.
Several options are available:
 From File(s):
Allows you to add image files from your pc or a server for use in the Arkite software.
Supported file types are: JPEG (.jpg, .jpeg), GIF (.gif), Bitmap (.bmp), PNG (.png), TIFF (.tiff, .tif),
SVG (.svg), STA (.sta) and STL (.stl)  to be used for a CAD/CAM detection
For video files, .mp4 and .mov are supported
 From Folder:
Allows you to add a folder from your pc. All image and video files from that folder will be added for
use in the Arkite software.
 From default images:
Allows you to add images from a library available to the Arkite software by default. It contains
images that are commonly used, e.g. tools, warnings, etc...
The images are in SVG format and can be used in different colors.

Images

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

 From RGB sensor:
Allows you to take a picture with any connected RGB camera, for example the one from the Arkite
3D sensor or a webcam. You have the option to crop the image before you save it.
 From RGB sensor (outline):
Allows you to take a before and an after snapshot with any connected RGB camera, for example
the one from the Arkite 3D sensor or a webcam. An outline image will be created containing only
the detected changes.
 From Phone:
Allows you to connect an Android phone to your workstation and directly send images or videos
from your phone to the Arkite software using the Arkite Companion app. When selecting this
option, a pop up with a QR code is displayed. With this QR code, you can download the Arkite
Companion app from the Google Play store. Once the Arkite Companion app is installed on your
phone, you can use the same QR code to connect your phone to the workstation. As long as your
phone is connected, you can keep sending images or videos to Arkite.
Note
You can also use a variable to define which image or video to show in the Image visualization. To
do so, click Proceed without selecting an image. In the properties of the Image visualization,
you can define the variable to use. For more information, refer to section 4.4.2 Visualization
properties on page 78.

Organizing your images and videos
A number of buttons are available to help you organize your images and videos:
 Right-click an image or video and select Delete to delete it.
 Select an image or video and drag it with your mouse to change its order.

 Select an image or video and click the button to create a subfolder and move the image or
video into it.
Once the subfolder exists, you can rename it and drag other images or videos into it.

 Select an image or video and click the button to move it up one folder.

 Click the button to expand all folders and subfolders.
 Click the button to collapse all folders and subfolders.

Images

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Editing images and videos
A number of buttons are available to edit images and videos you have added:

 Select an image and click to mirror it horizontally or click to mirror it vertically.

 Select an image and click to rotate it clockwise or click to rotate it counterclockwise.

 Select an image and click Replace Image to replace it.

 Select an image or video and click to adjust the cropping.
The Adjust cropping window appears. Set the zone you want to be visible and click OK.

When you add the image, only the selected zone will be visible.
Later, you can still change or remove the cropping. That change will be applied on all locations
where the image is used.

Images

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

 Select an image and click to remove its background.
The Remove background window appears. Set the zone from which you want to remove the
background and click Detect background.

Afterwards you can finetune the background detection. Click the black brush button and indicate
an area that is also part of the background but is not detected yet. Click the blue brush button
and indicate an area that is part of the object but was mistakenly detected as background.

When you are satisfied with the result, click Save Image.
A copy of the image without background is saved with the extension _bgremoved added to the
filename.

Color templates

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

15. Color templates

15.1 About color templates

Color templates can be used to define a visualizations color based on the value of a particular
variable. When changing or updating the template, all visualizations linked to the template will be
updated automatically.
Note
You can also define a visualizations color based on a variable without using templates. In that
case, changes need to be applied for every visualization separately. For more information, refer to
section Defining the color based on the value of a variable on page 106.

15.2 The Detection Colors template

By default, one color template called Detection colors is available in the Arkite software. This
template is used to define the colors of visualizations on a Projector display linked to a detection
during the execution of your assembly process.
To consult the Detection Colors template:
  1. In the ribbon, click the Color Templates button.
  2. In the Color Templates window, in the left pane, select Detection Colors.
  3. In the right pane, you can see the colors as defined for each status of the detection.
Note
  • In case the Alternate checkbox is checked, the color of the projection will alternate between
    the Primary Color and the Secondary Color. By default, the Secondary Color is
    transparent.
  • In case the Alternate checkbox is not checked, the Primary Color will always be used.
    The detections status is defined by the active step in the assembly..
Color templates

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

16. Languages and Translations

16.1 About languages and translations

The Arkite software allows you to define instructions, button labels and all other text elements in
different languages. This way, every operator can be supported in his or her own language while
executing a process.
By default, the Arkite software allows you to add instructions in English (en-us), but you can add as
many languages as you want.
Note
By default, instructions will be displayed in the language of the user that is running the project. If
no instructions are available in that language, the system will look for a similar language. For
example, if the user language is en-GB, en-US will be used. If no similar language is available, the
default language in the project will be used. For more information on defining the user language,
refer to section 17.4 Managing local users on page 277.

You can translate all instructions and text elements in your project using OpenAI. Translations are
always done from the default language. To translate from another language, first set that language as
your default language.

Warning
The translation feature works through an integration with OpenAI. This integration should be
enabled. To do so, navigate to Menu  Server  Settings  AI.
Enter the required configuration data:
  • OpenAI compatible server URL
  • AI model
  • API key you can use your own or contact support@arkite.com to obtain one.
  • Temperature: the default value 0 gives the best results for consistent translation of your
    instructions. However, it is not supported by all models.

16.2 Managing languages

Adding a language
To add a language:
  1. Click the Translations button in the ribbon.
Languages and Translations

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. Click the New Language button.
  2. Select a language from the list.
Tip
To quickly find a language, use the upper row to filter the list based on the languages Name ,
Native Name or Language Code.
  1. Select how the texts for the new language should be generated:
 Default: for detection steps, default text instructions will be generated. For other steps and
elements, the text fields will be empty.
Note
Default instructions are available for English, French, German, Dutch, Spanish and Italian.

 Copy: text elements will be copied from the language you select in the dropdown list.
 Translate: text elements will be translated from the language you select in the dropdown list.
  1. Click OK.
Deleting a language
To delete a language, right-click the column header for that language and select Delete Language.
Warning
  • All texts for that language will be deleted. If you add the language again later, you will have to
    re-implement any changes you made to default instructions or automatic translations.
  • You cannot delete the default language..
Setting a default language
To set the default language, select the language code from the dropdown list in the upper right corner.
The default language is used for showing instructions to users that have a user language that is not
available in the project and to generate automatic translations to other languages.

16.3 Managing Translations

Consulting and editing texts in your project
In the ribbon, click the Translations button.
The Translations window appears. It contains all text elements within the project in all configured
languages: text instructions, button labels, text visualizations,...
You can directly edit them in this overview.

Translating texts
You can translate all instructions and text elements in your project using OpenAI. Translations are
always done from the default language. To translate from another language, first set that language as
your default language.

Languages and Translations

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

Several options are possible:
 To translate a specific field, right-click the field in the table and select Translate from default.
 To translate only the empty fields, click the Translate button, select Empty fields and then the
language you want to translate.

 To translate everything, click the Translate button, select All fields and then the language you
want to translate.
Warning
Existing translations can be overwritten. If the field for the default language is empty, the fields for
the other languages will also be erased.
Fields for which the translation has been changed will be marked in orange until the Translations
window is closed.
Tip

You can also translate a text in the Properties of the corresponding control by clicking the
button.

Importing and exporting texts
You can export texts to let them translate outside of the Arkite software, for example by an external
party.
To export a language:
  1. Click the Export button.
  2. Select a Folder to export to.
  3. Select a Language to export, or select all languages.
  4. Click OK.
For each exported language, a file with extension .hdb is created. This file can be opened and edited
in Notepad++ or another text editor. After translation, you can import the file into the Arkite software
again.
  1. Click the Import button.
  2. Select a File to import.
  3. Select the correct Language.
  4. Click OK.
    The file is imported, and the instructions for the corresponding language in the project are updated.
User management

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

17. User management.......................................................................................................

17.1 About user management

Access to the Arkite software is granted through a username and password. That can either be a local
user created in the Arkite software, or an Active Directory user if Active Directory authentication has
been configured.
The actions that can be performed in the Arkite software depend on the role that is assigned to the
user or the Active Directory User Group. A role is a set of permissions.
Important
Users and roles are managed on server level. This means that a user that has been configured
can log in to the Arkite software on each workstation that is connected to the server.

17.2 Managing Authentication Settings......................................................................

What?
By default, users are created and managed locally in the Arkite software. However, you can also allow
authentication with an Active Directory user.

Configuring Active Directory Authentication
To configure Active Directory, execute the steps below:
  1. Click the Menu button.
  2. Click Users and then under Authentication click Settings.
  3. From the Authentication Method dropdown list, select Active directory users and local users.
  4. Specify the domaincontroller hostname, port, default domain and default external user language
    for your Active Directory setup.
Note
If a language is assigned to the user in Active Directory, this language will also be used in the
Arkite software. If no language is assigned in Active Directory, the language specified in the
Default External User Language field will be used.

User management

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. To test the connection, click the Test Authentication button.
  2. Provide an Active Directory user name and password and click Validate.
If the connection was successful, an authentication successful message will be shown.
  1. To fetch the user groups from your Active Directory, click Update External User Groups.
  2. Provide an Active Directory user name and password and click Validate.
    A message is shown with the number of found user groups.
  3. In the Authorized External User Groups list, indicate the user groups you want to grant access
    to the Arkite software and click OK.
Result
All Active Directory users that are part of an authorized user group will be able to login to the Arkite
software using their Active Directory login and password.
By default, an authorized Active Directory user will have read-only access to projects in status
Production , similar to the Operator user. To grant more permissions to the Active Directory user,
assign the external user group to a role.

17.3 Managing roles..................................................................................................

Default roles
By default, four roles are configured in the Arkite software:
 System Admin:
users with this role can edit settings and manage projects and users.
 User Manager:
users with this role can configure users and roles.
 Editor :
users with this role can edit projects and move them from Draft to Review and from Review to
Production (if no approval is required).
 Approver :
users with this role can do the same as editors, but can also approve or reject a project.
 View Sensor Streams:
users with this role can see the streams of the sensors (3D sensor, Vision sensor, RGB camera...)
in the Arkite software.

    Note
    An Active Directory user will only have access to the software if the selected user group or another

  1. Click Menu.
  2. Click Users.
  3. Click the role you want to edit.
  4. Update the name, description and permissions of the role as required.
    If you want to delete the role, click the Delete Role button.
Note
The default roles cannot be deleted nor edited. This way, you cannot accidentally lock yourself out
of the application.

Creating local users

User management

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

  1. Provide a username and (optionally) a password for the new user and click OK.
  2. Select a language for the user.
    Text instructions from all projects will be shown in this language when this user is logged in.
    Note
    If no instructions are available in the users language, the system will first check if there are
    instructions available in a language with the same primary language subtag. If this is not the
    case, the system will fall back to en-US as a default language.
    For example, if users language is fr-BE and no instructions are available in that language,
    instructions will be shown in fr-FR if available. Otherwise, en-US will be used.

    user.
Note
For every user that is added, the system automatically generates an API key. This key is used to
authenticate when accessing the Arkite API. You can let the system generate a new key by
clicking the Refresh API Key button. When you do so, existing functionality will not work anymore
though.

The Arkite API

Arkite NV C-Mine 12, 3600 Genk, Belgium W: http://www.arkite.com TEL: +32 (0) 89 201 745 - MAIL: info@arkite.com

18. The Arkite API

18.1 About the Arkite API

The Arkite software has a flexible Application Programming Interface (API) that allows swift
communication with other software applications in the software ecosystem of the manufacturer like
MES and ERP systems.
This API can be used to push data from MES into the Arkite software in order to enable the on-
demand flexible production. This integration will avoid stock pile-up and can benefit from the fact that
the Arkite software is flexible to be programmed to deal with product variants on the fly.
It contains rest calls for retrieving and modifying project data, as well as a number of calls to run
operations on a currently running workstation.

18.2 API examples

The Arkite API can be used for example to:

 Schedule tasks on a workstation when an order is received by your ERP system
 Load a project on a specific workstation when a new workday starts
 Update the picking bin content from your WMS system

 Get the status of a detection
 Add a variant
 ...
Note
For most entities in the Arkite software, an object ID is displayed next to the label of the Name
property on the Properties pane. In the Workstations overview, the workstations object ID is
shown in the Workstation ID column. You can copy it to use it when working with the Arkite API.

18.3 More information

Extended documentation of the Arkite API can be found on SwaggerHub:
https://app.swaggerhub.com/apis-docs/Arkite/ArkiteAPI/2025.1
For testing, you can use the Open API Tester. To access this page, click the API Tester button in the
ribbon of the software.

This is a offline tool, your data stays locally and is not send to any server!
